# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-07-04 (previous): **D244 — E13+E41 save hardening SHIPPED: a tampered autosave can no longer brick the game, and the save-shape law now has structural teeth in the build.**

**Newest (D244):** two quiet integrity holes are closed. **E13:** a hand-tampered autosave (an own `hasOwnProperty` key smuggled into settings) used to crash the engine at script-evaluation time — the whole game died at boot and stayed dead until localStorage was cleared. A new guarded override module (`src/105-save-guard.js`) now rejects that payload at load (it reads as "no save", the same posture the D234 slot lanes already took) and sanitizes it at apply (never throws, never lets the poison key land where the engine would later call it); every legitimate save behaves byte-identically, and the negative control proves the teeth bite — the pre-fix build served with the tamper dies with three pageerrors, the fixed build boots clean and rejects it. **E41:** the architecture law "save changes need a `_SAVE_VER` bump with lazy migration, or must be purely additive" is now enforced by the build itself: a new gate hashes the seven save-envelope-owning functions against a tracked manifest (`tools/save-shape.json`), mirrors `_SAVE_VER`, refuses disarming/dead-copy/assignment-form evasions, and fails any drift until the bump-or-additive decision is made consciously in the same commit — proven firing on five violation fixtures. probe-save-slots grew 4 teeth (14/14); two slow-Mac harness flakes repaired the documented D232/D233 way (no assertion touched). 3-lens Opus panel, default-refute: 3× SAFE_TO_COMMIT; its one real find is a PRE-EXISTING navigation-gated residual (tampered `campaign.*` sub-objects), filed honestly as new ledger item **E50** rather than scope-crept into this slice.

**Queue (Aaron-locked, D237/D238, updated): S25 palette next → battle-mode-parity arc** (its pacing A/B assumed E47 fully landed — note the half-landed state) **→ E48 + E49 (both APPROVED 2026-07-04: buzzer rule + surrender/straggler design session) → then the Shiloh/Gettysburg flips complete E47 and the Piper guns complete E46.** All locks stand (Phase H parked D214; M8-battle-build/Q5/Q6 locked; Phase D deferred).

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-30: **GRADUATE-HISTORY PASS M1 SHIPPED — CORRECTIONS & FABRICATION FIX (D180).**

**Newest (D180, 2026-06-30):** a new authorized multi-milestone build-out (brief `.tmp/civil-war-phd-execution-brief.md`; audit `.tmp/civil-war-history-audit-and-phd-plan.md`; Native dossier `.tmp/native-nations-under-told-dossier.md`) raises the game's history toward a graduate-seminar bar. **M1** ships the audit's Phase-1 corrections on a clean base and fixes the one integrity defect: the twenty-slave-law teaching card in `data/decisions.json` shipped dramatized composite voices in verbatim-quote style (untagged) — including a padded Sam Watkins line and an invented first-person "enslaved" voice — all under `provenance:"Verified"`. Now every composite is tagged `[composite illustration — not a verbatim quotation]`, Watkins is trimmed to the exact 1882 *Co. Aytch* clause, and the invented enslaved voice is replaced with a real, verbatim, ≥2-source-verified Cpl. James Henry Gooding 1863 excerpt (the first real Black voice in verified words on a player-facing card).

**What else changed:** Erlanger "72%"→"~45% of face" (economy.json), Vicksburg date standardized to May 18 + clause, the manpower CS replacement-ratio fallback reframed as a model parameter, the `confederate-greenbacks-inflation` codex id renamed to `greenbacks-and-wartime-inflation` (4 refs lockstep), the Mississippi Declaration date fixed to Jan. 9 1861 (HISTORICAL-DATA.md), and the Cornerstone quote hyphenated to "corner-stone" (commas kept). Pure teaching read-out, **D74 byte-identical**, anti-Lost-Cause.

**Verified:** build **GATE OK** (no-fudge ✓, citations ✓); focused `probe-decisions` 19/0, `probe-economy` 8/0, `probe-codex` 18/0; adjacent `probe-manpower` 9/0, `probe-vicksburg` 18/0; all 0 pageerrors; `git diff --check` clean. Full `npm run vet:noreg` deferred under D176.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-29: **PHASE F POW EXCHANGE CARTEL COLLAPSE IS FOCUSED-GATED. Prisoner exchange, camp pressure, and relief priority are live with exact-zero default bridge behavior.**

**Current (D161, 2026-06-29):** This is the bounded POW exchange-collapse slice after D159 rail logistics. New `data/prisoner-exchange.json` and `src/62-prisoner-exchange.js` add a War Effort prisoner/camp surface tied to resolved-battle capture estimates, year/stage pressure, and an explicit relief priority. It does not start Chattanooga, does not start USCT playable battles, does not hand-edit `build/base.html`, and does not change the save version. `civil_war_generals.html` was rebuilt from `src/` by the build gate.

**What changed:** War Effort now shows **Prisoner Exchange & Camps**: pressure, exchange function, detained burden, camp mortality risk, side policy, timeline, camp notes, source/debate cards, and a **Prioritize relief** toggle. The toggle is the only bridge activator. Default/inactive POW relief returns exact zero; active effects are capped at morale +2, fatigue relief 2, supply cost 2, and overall +1. Relief can mitigate deaths/returns and a small returned-prisoner manpower boost, but it never reopens the cartel.

**Source guardrail:** the existing history/codex source trail was sufficient, so no web fetch was needed. The module teaches the Dix-Hill cartel, Confederate threats against captured Black soldiers, Lincoln's retaliation order, Andersonville, Elmira, and camp overcrowding. It names suffering on both sides without treating cartel collapse as neutral or erasing slavery and USCT status.

**Verified:** syntax checks passed; build GATE OK; importer/schema checks passed; focused `probe-prisoner-exchange` 8/8 with 0 pageerrors; adjacent probes passed for logistics rail, manpower, bridge, and desk; corrected screenshot readback showed the active POW block without overlap. A full no-regression run was started and passed through `probe-divergence` with all completed probes green and 0 pageerrors, then Aaron stopped it and deferred the rest to the planned-work batch/release gate.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-27: **MODEL ROUTING, UI-REDESIGN LAW, AND THE NORMAL NO-REGRESSION GATE ARE SHIPPED. The next clean work is Phase J save/share hardening, then Phase I loot/survival.**

**Newest (D145, 2026-06-27):** This is a blocker-clearing docs/tooling milestone before new gameplay. It does not change how the game plays. It changes what future agents are allowed to assume and how they verify work.

**What changed:** the repo now says the main reasoning/integration loop stays on **5.5** for architecture, important code, user-facing text, historical judgment, UI/UX decisions, accessibility judgment, bug hunts, final review, and irreversible or quality-critical work. Smaller/token-efficient helpers are only for bounded packets like search summaries, inventories, probe-log summaries, mechanical doc syncs, exact-schema cleanup, first-pass gathering, and repetitive fixture/probe scaffolding; every helper call must explicitly set model and effort.

**The UI direction is now real roadmap work:** D145 supersedes "broadsheet everywhere." The future shell should feel more like a historical command game: brighter, rounder, more dramatic, icon-led, and centered on public-domain photos/illustrations where they clarify people, places, or stakes. Broadsheet stays for press/editorial/dispatch/provenance surfaces. The constraints stay strict: Civil War gravity, anti-Lost-Cause framing, WCAG 2.2 AA, keyboard support, reduced motion, CVD-safe cues, no unclear-license assets, and the Intel UHD-617 performance floor. Research notes are in `docs/design/ui-redesign-research.md`; `V1-CHECKLIST.md` now has a concrete H0 redesign task.

**The gate is now real:** `npm run vet:noreg` runs the normal no-regression suite through `tools/vet-no-regression.mjs`, including the D143 full-campaign probe and `diag-classic`. The runner serializes probes, checks JSON `ok`/pageerror summaries, writes a timestamped log under `.tmp/`, and kills timed-out child process groups so a wedged Chrome probe fails cleanly. The audit found useful failures: an accessibility static-scan false-red, a `bootprobe` browser-close hang, a `probe-phased-3d` hang, and render-richness/weather/tactical-visuals needing honest heavy-probe budgets or scene isolation. Those are fixed or budgeted.

**Verified:** build GATE OK; focused accessibility 25/25; phased-3D 64/64; render-richness 30/30; weather 30/30; final no-regression segment from weather through full-campaign and Classic green; `probe-full-campaign` 4/4 with 0 pageerrors; `diag-classic` `nonBlank:346`, `m3dActive:false`; no pageerrors in the completed gate. **Next:** Phase J save/mod/share hardening, then Phase I loot/survival. Chattanooga and the USCT playable battles still stay saved for last.

The new full-campaign probe drives the generated game in Chrome, auto-resolves every campaign battle through the real battle bridge, steps through the President's between-battle screen, and keeps going until the final report renders.

**What it proves:** the Union chain resolves all 31 battles from `sumter` to `appomattox`, and the Confederate chain resolves all 28. Each step has to advance the campaign cleanly, record the completed battle, clear recovery state, and show the interstitial. The probe also checks two fragile branches: losing a battle and replaying it in recovery mode, and accepting an early negotiated peace when the war can be concluded. Both still land on the graded final report instead of leaving the campaign half-alive.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-26: **THE MODERN BATTLEFIELD NOW HAS REAL FIELDWORKS — brigades no longer just "dig in" as a flat bonus. They scrape rifle pits, build hasty cover, raise full parapets, and finally stand behind redoubts and earthworks that protect the front, help less on the flank, and can be bypassed from the rear. Abatis is nastier when tied to prepared works. And when you order a charge, the men now get a short correction window, then commit until contact or the target is lost.**

**Newest (D142, 2026-06-26):** This closes the Ultimate-General-fidelity push you set for the modern engine. The fortification system is deeper now: the HUD tells you what stage your works are in and how much front cover they give; the top-down and 3D views draw the earthworks as they grow; and the cover actually cares which direction the fire comes from. A frontal attack into a redoubt is ugly. A flank or rear approach still matters. Abatis built out in the open is still useful, but abatis tied to a prepared parapet/redoubt is visibly heavier, slows more, shocks the men harder, and takes longer to clear.

**The terrain from the last step now bites too.** Swamp, town, and fort were made visible in D141; in this pass they were wired into the universal movement/cover hooks. Swamps slow troops hard and give only soft concealment, towns give hard cover but slow movement, and forts give the strongest cover while making an attacker cross the ditch/parapet friction. No battle got a special damage rule — this is one shared model.

**The careful part:** because this changes tactics, it is a D74 gameplay carve-out, not a byte-identical presentation pass. I still kept the AI and the universal model honest: AI charges remain unchanged, no per-battle outcome fudge was added, and the preset/phased A/B guards stayed green. The bug-hunt found one real edge case — committed charges were supposed to unlock if the charging unit routed or died, but the predicate only checked the target. Fixed and probed. **Verified:** build GATE OK; focused probes for engineering, terrain, order feel, and Bull Run all green; presets 26/26; phased A/B 20 comparisons with 0 diffs; full no-regression passed after the fix; Classic still paints at `nonBlank:346`; 0 pageerrors. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** H2 reenactment-footage decision or Phase I/J polish. Chattanooga and the USCT playable battles still stay saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-26: **YOU CAN NOW READ THE GROUND — the third step of the big goal you set. In the modern engine, high ground and low ground are finally obvious at a glance, and you can pick HOW you see it: soft hillshade (the default), drawn contour lines with elevation numbers, or a color-by-height map — switch any time with the R key, the in-battle Settings, or the new little "Terrain" panel in the corner. Hover anywhere and it tells you the exact height and what's underfoot ("+18 yd · rise · Woods"). And every kind of ground now looks distinct — including the three new ones you asked for: swamp, town, and fort.**

**Newest (D141, 2026-06-26):** You set the goal that the modern engine should look *and* play better than Ultimate General: Gettysburg, and after the movement (D139) and the richer look (D140), the next step we agreed on was making the **terrain itself readable** — so that's this. I asked you three quick questions and you chose: use the **Viridis** color scale (the one that's safe for color-blindness), keep a **small always-on legend** in the corner, and **add swamp, town, and fort** as their own distinct terrain (not just label the ones already there). So now: high/low ground reads instantly; you have three ways to view elevation and can flip between them instantly; a corner panel shows the height scale, a live read-out of whatever you're pointing at, and a key to every terrain type on the field; the simple top-down view finally shows hills and hollows (it was flat green before); and swamps, towns, and forts each have their own look.

**The careful part — it changes nothing in the fighting.** Like the richer-look step, this is **pure presentation**: it only draws pixels, never touches the rules, the dice, or your save. The swamp/town/fort are *visual only* for now (we agreed their cover/movement effects come later) — so the battles still play **exactly** as before, proven bit-for-bit (the difficulty test 26/26 and the head-to-head 20/20 identical). A brand-new readability test (26 checks) confirms all three view-modes work, the legend and hover read-out are correct, every terrain type is named, the colors are color-blind-safe, and turning things off cleanly reverts. The bug-hunt — 43 reviewers across six angles — found a handful of real things and I **fixed every one** before committing: the contour lines were being redrawn far too often (a speed drain on weaker machines — now drawn once and reused); the keyboard could lose its place when you clicked the legend (fixed); and the corner panel's terrain key could go stale when a multi-day battle moved to new ground (now it refreshes). **Verified:** build OK; the new test 26/26; the fighting untouched; the 3D battlefield still healthy; the classic view still paints; accessibility AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the last piece of the modern-engine push — **deeper fortifications** (richer entrenchments/earthworks, and the "commit to the charge" lock we deferred earlier; it's also where swamp/town/fort would gain their real cover effects). Chattanooga and the USCT *battles* stay saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE MODERN BATTLEFIELD NOW LOOKS THE PART — the second step of the big goal you set. The ground reads in real 3D relief (low ground sinks darker, the crests catch the light), every brigade now sits in a soft shadow on the field instead of floating above it, the sky deepens overhead with a gentle cinematic vignette framing the action, and each unit block carries painted ranks of men (with little 3D figures standing on top, on stronger machines) so it reads as a body of troops, not a flat tile.**

**Newest (D140, 2026-06-25):** You set the goal that the modern engine should look *and* play better than Ultimate General: Gettysburg, and after the movement work (D139) we agreed the next step was making it **look** the part — the "polished hybrid" style. That's this. I asked you three quick questions and you chose: go **all-in** (the full look plus the little 3D figure-ranks on capable machines), **keep the existing antique colours** rather than flip a risky global "film look," and make the high/low ground **clearly** readable. So the field now has genuine relief shading (you can read a ridge from a hollow at a glance), a soft contact-shadow grounds every brigade, the flat sky became a deepening dome with a faint vignette, and the unit markers wear stylized ranks of infantry.

**Why I didn't flip the "cinematic film look":** the game's 3D library is an older version, and turning on that global film-colour mode would have broken in an ugly way — the gunsmoke and rain are drawn by a different path that *wouldn't* get the new look, so they'd suddenly clash with everything else, and I'd have had to re-tune every colour in four files for a palette that already looks right. A team of reviewers confirmed it. So I got the richer look by *adding* depth (shadows, relief, sky, troop detail) on top of the colours you already have — which is safer and keeps the period feel.

**The careful part — it changes nothing in the fighting.** Unlike the movement step (which deliberately touched how troops move), this is **pure looks**: it only ever changes pixels, never the rules, the dice, or your save. I proved that the battles play **exactly** as before — the difficulty test came back 26-for-26 identical and the head-to-head 20-for-20 identical, on the final build — and a brand-new looks-test (26 checks) confirms the relief, the grounded shadows, the dome, the vignette, and the troop detail all appear, that turning enrichment "off" cleanly reverts to the old plain look, and that none of it touches the dice. The bug-hunt — 19 reviewers across six angles — came back **"safe to commit"** with nothing to fix; I applied two small forward-looking polish tweaks it suggested anyway (so the 3D figures scale efficiently for the bigger battles still to come). **Verified:** build OK; the new looks-test 26/26; the fighting untouched (26/26 and 20-for-20); the smoke/weather/flag 3D tests still pass; the classic view still paints; accessibility fine. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the rest of the modern-engine push, in order — making **high and low ground explicit** (a hillshade/contour-lines toggle with a legend and a hover read-out), then **deeper fortifications**. Chattanooga and the USCT *battles* stay saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE MODERN BATTLES NOW MOVE LIKE ULTIMATE GENERAL — this is the first step of the big goal you set. In the modern (non-hex) engine you now command troops the fluid way: click a brigade, then click where it should stand and drag to aim which way it faces; drag a unit onto an enemy to charge that very brigade; hold Shift to chain a march route waypoint by waypoint; and a live "ghost" shows exactly where the men will go, which way they'll face, and what the order is — in both the simple top-down view and the full 3D. Digging in is faster now too.**

**Newest (D139, 2026-06-25):** You set the goal that the modern engine should look and *play* better than Ultimate General: Gettysburg, and we agreed to build the **movement and ordering feel first** — so that's what this is. The four things you chose are all in: **(1)** orders take effect immediately, but **hold Shift** to queue up a planned route; **(2)** to charge, you **drag a brigade right onto the enemy you want it to hit** (before, it only ever charged whichever foe was nearest); **(3)** the **"point, then aim" handle** — tap a spot to send the men there facing the way they already face, or drag to swing a little arrow and set their facing, and you can grab that arrow later to re-aim a unit that's already marching; **(4)** **digging in is faster** (a full parapet now forms in about 42 seconds instead of 70). And the whole time there's a **live ghost preview** so you can see the order before you commit it. The hex game ("Classic") is **completely untouched** — it stays exactly as it was.

**The careful part:** changing how troops move is the one place we agreed could change the game's feel (everything else this year was proven "bit-for-bit identical"). So I built it to touch *only your controls* — never the computer opponent's brain. That let me prove the actual fighting still plays **exactly the same as before** (the head-to-head test came back 20-for-20 identical, and the difficulty test 26-for-26), while a brand-new test drives the new gestures and confirms they each do the right thing. The bug-hunt — 31 reviewers across six angles — came back **"safe to commit"** with nothing blocking; I went ahead and fixed four small polish items it found anyway (so the order ghost reads by *shape* and not just color for colorblind players, and the 3D ghost layers cleanly). **Verified:** build OK; the new movement test 12/12; the fighting untouched (26/26 and 20-for-20); the 3D battlefield healthy; the classic view still paints; accessibility AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the rest of the modern-engine push, in order — making it **look** richer (the polished hybrid style), then making **high and low ground obvious** (the hillshade/contour-lines toggle with a legend and hover readout), then **deeper fortifications**. Chattanooga and the USCT *battles* stay saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE BATTLEFIELDS NOW HAVE FACES TOO — before each battle, the briefing screen now shows a famous real photograph of that actual field: the Confederate dead in the "Bloody Lane" at Antietam, the dead on the field at Gettysburg ("A Harvest of Death"), the dead behind the stone wall at Marye's Heights, the pontoon bridges over the Rappahannock at Fredericksburg, the dug-in siege lines at Vicksburg, and Sudley Ford at Bull Run. AND you set the next big goal: make the modern battle engine look and play better than Ultimate General: Gettysburg.**

Six of the nine big battles now have one; for three (Malvern Hill, Shiloh, Chickamauga) no clean period photograph of the field exists, so those briefings stay as they were — and I wrote down exactly why. **Looking at every picture first paid off again:** three of the first results weren't photographs at all — a 1917 *drawn* bird's-eye panorama of Shiloh, a colored battle *map* of Chickamauga, and a book *engraving* of steamers at the landing — all thrown out. The ones I kept are the genuine wartime photographs, matched carefully to the right field, and three of them are photographs of the dead — shown plainly and with respect, named for the cost they were, never glorified. It changes nothing in the fighting (proven bit-for-bit), and the bug-hunt came back "safe to commit" with one small fix (the Gettysburg picture's credit now correctly reads the Smithsonian, which is where that scan is held). **Verified:** build OK, the new scenes test 16/16, the fighting untouched (26/26 + 20-for-20), the 3D battlefield healthy, accessibility AA. Committed + pushed.

**And the bigger thing — your direction, now locked in:** you told me the **modern engine must look *and* play better than Ultimate General: Gettysburg on PS4.** I've written it into the plan and my memory so it carries across every future session. The shape: the **hex map stays exactly as it is — that's Classic.** The **modern engine gets no hex boxes** — it should move and fight fluidly like UG:G, with **drag-and-click direct orders** for movement and charges, formation facing, and an option to **fortify/entrench.** We settled four things: build the **movement-and-ordering *feel* first**; aim for a **polished hybrid look** (rich 3D terrain with stylized troops/flags, not heavy 3D models); make **high and low ground explicit** with a **shading-or-lines toggle** (default soft hillshade, switchable to contour lines or color-by-height, plus a legend and a hover readout) and every terrain type clearly distinct; and keep it a **self-contained file with an optional downloadable HD pack** for maximum fidelity. That's the next major arc.

**Next:** start the modern engine's **movement & ordering feel** — the UG:G-style drag/click/direct controls + fortify. Chattanooga and the USCT *battles* stay saved for last.)

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE LEADERS NOW HAVE FACES — open any "People" entry in the Codex and you now see that person's real wartime photograph: Lincoln standing in the field at Antietam, Grant leaning against a tree at his Cold Harbor headquarters, Lee, Jefferson Davis, Sherman, Stonewall Jackson, Longstreet, McClellan, Meade, "the Rock of Chickamauga" George Thomas, Sheridan, Bragg, Cleburne, Admiral Farragut, Stanton, Seward, Stephens, Clara Barton, Dorothea Dix, and Dr. Mary Walker**

**Newest (overnight run, D136):** Continuing the public-domain imagery in the hands-off way you asked for, I gave the Codex's "People" entries their faces. Twenty-four people have entries; four already showed a photo from the U.S. Colored Troops work (Douglass, Tubman, Shaw, and the Fort Pillow entry). I sourced, checked, and embedded a famous wartime photograph for the **other twenty leaders** — and chose "leader in the field" pictures wherever a great one exists: Lincoln among the officers' tents at Antietam in 1862, Grant standing by a tree at his Cold Harbor headquarters. Each picture carries a written description and a caption naming the person and the archive it comes from, and the captions tell the truth plainly — Stephens' "Cornerstone Speech" that called slavery the new government's foundation, Cleburne's 1864 proposal to arm and free enslaved men (for which he was never promoted again), Longstreet smeared by the Lost Cause writers, Thomas the Virginian who stayed loyal to the Union.

**Looking at every picture first paid off — again, even more than last time.** I checked each candidate image with my own eyes before baking it in, and that caught **eleven wrong pictures out of twenty.** The worst: the picture the search returned for "Jefferson Davis" was actually a *different man of the same name* — a **Union general, Jefferson C. Davis** — not the Confederate president (the same trap as the "Shaw" mix-up last time); the "Stanton" was a photograph of a Black Union soldier with his wife and daughters; the "Seward" was his teenage daughter Fanny; several were group photos or old engravings instead of a clean portrait; and "Grant" was a newspaper *drawing*, not the photograph. All eleven were thrown out and replaced with the genuine article, which I then looked at again to confirm.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only adds a picture to a teaching card — a test proves the battles and the campaign play bit-for-bit the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, or your save). **The bug-hunt came back "safe to commit" with nothing to fix:** one reviewer re-checked every picture's public-domain licence live (all twenty clean), another looked at each picture and confirmed the right person with no wrong dates or fake "photographs," and a final reviewer independently re-examined the six riskiest ones and signed off. I also found and fixed a small flaw the *last* imagery work had left in one of the tests (it wrongly assumed the Codex would never contain any picture — true before, false now). **Verified:** build OK; the new leaders-imagery test 15/15; the Codex test 18/18; the fighting untouched (26/26 byte-identity and a 20-for-20 head-to-head); the 3D battlefield still healthy (flag, weather, render, and audio tests all pass); accessibility AA. (A few of the heaviest 3D tests stalled on this 8 GB Mac's memory while Blender was open — not a regression, since this change never touches the 3D code and four other full 3D tests pass.) Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the battlefield *scenes* — the famous Gardner and Brady photographs of the actual fields — on the pre-battle briefing screen (I kept those separate so the somber ones get their own careful pass), or the real surviving regimental colours as a teaching display, then the reenactment footage. Chattanooga and the USCT *battles* (the playable scenarios) remain saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE U.S. COLORED TROOPS NOW HAVE FACES — the teaching cards now show the real, famous photographs of the United States Colored Troops and the people of their story: a whole company of the 4th U.S. Colored Infantry drawn up at their fort, Sergeant William Carney holding the flag he saved at Fort Wagner, Colonel Robert Gould Shaw, Frederick Douglass, Harriet Tubman, the period newspaper engraving of the Fort Pillow massacre, and the "Come and Join Us Brothers" recruiting poster**

**Newest (overnight run, D135):** Continuing the public-domain imagery in the "hands-off, edge-cases only" way you asked for, I sourced, vetted, and embedded a set of real period photographs of the U.S. Colored Troops and wired them into the parts of the game that already teach that history — the Codex entries and the "The Ranks" manpower panel. Open the Codex entry for the United States Colored Troops and you now see the famous photograph of Company E of the 4th U.S. Colored Infantry standing at their fort outside Washington; the 54th Massachusetts entry shows Sergeant William Carney holding the flag he carried up the parapet at Fort Wagner (the deed that made him the first Black Medal of Honor soldier); and Colonel Shaw, Frederick Douglass, and Harriet Tubman each appear on their own entries. For Nathan Bedford Forrest's entry I deliberately did **not** put up a flattering portrait of the man — instead it shows the 1864 newspaper engraving of the Fort Pillow massacre, which keeps the focus where it belongs: on the surrendering Black soldiers who were killed. And once you organize the USCT in a campaign, "The Ranks" panel shows the 1863 "Come and Join Us Brothers" recruiting poster. Every picture is public-domain, sourced and credited, and — unlike the weapon cut-outs — each carries a written description and a caption naming the subject and the archive it comes from, because these photographs *are* the teaching, not just decoration.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only adds pictures to the teaching cards — a test proves the battles and the campaign play exactly the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, or your save). **I looked at every image myself before baking it in — and that caught a real mistake:** the first "Robert Gould Shaw" picture I pulled turned out to be a *later man of the same name* (a relative, in an early-1900s striped suit), not the Civil War colonel — so I threw it out and found the genuine wartime portrait of him in uniform. **The bug-hunt — six angles, one of which re-checks every licence live and another that actually looks at each picture — came back "safe to commit"** and found three small things, all fixed: the little credit line under each caption was a touch too faint to meet the accessibility contrast bar (now darkened and verified), and two record-keeping notes about the Tubman photograph's date and pose were off (the photo is actually just-postwar, and she's seated, not standing — the caption players actually see was already correct). **Verified:** build OK; the new USCT-imagery test 17/17; the fighting and campaign untouched (26/26 byte-identity); the portrait, weapon, smoke, weather, render, audio, flag, and 3D tests all still pass; accessibility AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** more public-domain imagery in the same hands-off way — likely the battlefield scenes and the leaders in the field (the famous Brady and Gardner photographs), or the real surviving regimental colours as a teaching display — then, eventually, the reenactment footage. # ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE GUNS NOW HAVE FACES — the Armory and Cannon-Corps cards now show real public-domain photographs of the actual weapons and field guns: the Springfield, Enfield, Sharps, Spencer, Henry, Colt, Lorenz, and old 1842 musket each as a clean Smithsonian studio cut-out; the 12-pdr Napoleon as a genuine Civil-War artist's pencil sketch; and the Whitworth as a period photograph with its crew**

The Armory now shows each gun for sale as its actual photograph: the small arms are crisp Smithsonian museum cut-outs (the gun floating on the card, no box), the 12-pounder Napoleon is a real pencil sketch a Civil-War combat artist drew at the Rappahannock in 1863, and the Whitworth is a wartime photograph of the gun and its crew. Every image is sourced to a public-domain repository, its licence recorded, and its accuracy checked. **10 of the 14 models got a photo; 4 were left without one on purpose** — for two of them (the Richmond rifle and the old 1841 howitzer) no clean public-domain picture exists, and for the other two the only candidates were *wrong* (more on that below), so their cards simply stay as they were.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only adds a picture to a card — a test proves the battles and the armory math play exactly the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, the purchase logic, or your save). **The bug-hunt earned its keep — twice over.** A team of six AI reviewers, one of which actually *looks at* each image and another that re-checks each licence live, caught two real howlers I'd embedded by mistake: the "10-pounder Parrott" card was showing a giant 200-pounder *fortress* gun (the wrong class entirely), and the "3-inch Ordnance Rifle" was a *modern* color snapshot of a monument on a snowy town square with cars and traffic lights in the background. Both were thrown out (those cards now show no photo rather than a wrong one). It also caught that the Henry rifle was rendering as an ugly box and swapped it for a clean cut-out, fixed a file-format trap in the build tool, and made the card images properly invisible to screen-readers (since the gun's name is already written right beside it). A final reviewer looked at all ten surviving images one more time and signed off. **Verified:** build OK; the new arms-imagery test 17/17; the fighting and the armory untouched (26/26 byte-identity, the weapon and cannon math tests pass); the portrait, smoke, weather, render, audio, flag, and 3D tests all still pass; accessibility AA. # ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE REAL PHOTOS NOW TRAVEL WITH THE GAME — the generals' actual period photographs now show up even when you open the game file on its own, with nothing else around it. Before, the real photos only appeared when the game sat next to its picture folder; moved or downloaded by itself, it fell back to the drawn engravings. Now a small, compressed copy of every portrait is baked right into the single file, so Lincoln, Lee, Grant, and the rest look like their real selves anywhere you open it**

**Newest (overnight run, D133):** You chose to start the public-domain imagery work ("Go on H1/H2 now"), and this first step builds the *machinery* for it and proves it on the photographs we already have. The game has 155 real period photographs of the generals and cabinet (all public domain, gathered earlier), but they were stored as separate picture files *beside* the game — so the moment you moved the single game file somewhere on its own, the photos vanished and you saw the hand-drawn engravings instead. This builds a proper pipeline: it shrinks each photo to a small thumbnail and bakes those right into the one game file, then teaches the game to prefer the sharp original when the picture folder is present, fall back to the baked-in photo when it isn't, and only then fall back to the engraving. The file grew from about 3 to 4.3 megabytes — a fair trade for portraits that travel anywhere. Each portrait is shown in the same period brass-oval frame as before, so nothing looks out of place.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes which picture shows in a frame — a test proves the battles play bit-for-bit the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, or your save). **The bug-hunt — six angles of attack — earned its keep:** it caught that when the picture folder *was* present, the new code could quietly swap the sharp original down to the smaller baked-in copy on a general's badge in battle (now it leaves any real photo alone); that baking all 155 thumbnails at startup was wasted work when the sharp originals were already there (now it only bakes them when it detects the game is running on its own); and three smaller build-tool robustness points. A final reviewer signed it off as safe. **Honest scope:** this makes the *portraits* travel with the file; the 3D battlefield's ground textures and sky still load from their folder — those are the next imagery steps. **Verified:** build OK; the new portrait test 22/22 (including a check that opens the file with the picture folder *blocked* and confirms the photo still shows); the fighting untouched (26/26 byte-identity, and a 20-for-20 head-to-head); the smoke, weather, render, audio, flag, and 3D tests all still pass; the classic view still paints. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the rest of the public-domain imagery — photos of the weapons, the flags, the U.S. Colored Troops, and battle scenes — then the reenactment footage. Each of those pulls in *new* outside pictures, so I'll show you each batch for your sign-off before baking it in. A "weather that shifts between the stages of a battle" idea is also still queued. Chattanooga and the USCT battles remain saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE MULTI-DAY BATTLES NOW WORK RIGHT IN 3D — when a big battle like Antietam, Gettysburg, Chickamauga, or Vicksburg moves from one stage to the next, the 3D battlefield finally rebuilds itself: the new troops appear, the old ones are cleared away, and the woods and the objective flag move to the new part of the field (before, the next stage showed an empty field)**

**Newest (overnight run, D132):** You chose this fix over the public-domain photo layer (which has to wait until you're around to approve each image). It repairs a real, pre-existing bug that the *last* run's bug-hunt had spotted and flagged for a dedicated fix. Four of the battles are fought in several stages — Antietam moves from the Cornfield to the Sunken Road to Burnside's Bridge; Gettysburg across its three days; and Chickamauga and the Vicksburg siege likewise — and each stage is a different patch of ground with different troops and a different objective. In the full 3D view, when a battle moved to its next stage, the game swapped in the new troops and the new ground *in the rules* but never rebuilt the *picture* — so the new brigades were invisible, the old ones lingered as ghosts, and the trees and the golden objective marker stayed stuck on the previous stage's field. (The simple top-down view was always fine; this only ever affected the 3D view of a multi-stage battle.) Now the 3D field rebuilds cleanly at each stage: the new brigades appear, everything from the last stage is properly cleared, the woods and walls and objective marker move to the new ground, and the camera swings around to face the new sector.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes the 3D *picture* — a test proves the battles play bit-for-bit the same as before (a head-to-head of all four multi-stage battles across five starting seeds came back identical to the letter — same winner, same casualties, same everything; the fix never runs during the behind-the-scenes calculations, only when you're watching in 3D). **The bug-hunt — six angles of attack — earned its keep:** it found that rebuilding the scene was *leaking memory* — the trenches, obstacles, and pontoon bridges from the old stage weren't being thrown away (most visible in the Vicksburg siege), and an old river could linger if the next stage had none. Both were fixed (the scene now disposes of everything from the previous stage), plus a third nicety so that if a rebuild ever did go wrong it would announce itself instead of silently leaving an empty field. **Verified:** build OK; the new multi-stage 3D test 64/64 across all four battles; the fighting untouched (the difficulty test 26/26 and the head-to-head 20-for-20 identical); the smoke, weather, render, audio, and flag tests all still pass; the top-down classic view still paints; the victory screen at Burnside's Bridge now shows the real field instead of an empty one. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the public-domain photo and reenactment-footage layer — but only with your sign-off first, because it pulls in outside images (and any outside sound files are the same kind of decision). A "weather that shifts between the stages of a battle" idea is also queued. Chattanooga and the USCT battles are still saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **EVERY BRIGADE NOW FLIES THE RIGHT FLAG — each unit carries the colours its history records (the Confederates' "Stars and Bars" at Bull Run, the famous red Southern-Cross battle flag later in the East, the blue-and-white-moon Western flag in Tennessee), and the Union corps now wear their real badges — the disc, the clover, the diamond, the crosses — but only at the 1863 battles where those badges were actually worn**

**Newest (overnight run, D131):** The battlefield's flags and insignia got a deep, history-accurate pass. Each brigade now flies the flag its army actually carried, *when* it carried it. The big teaching beat: at **First Bull Run (1861) the Confederates fly the "Stars and Bars" national flag — not the famous red battle flag**, because that battle flag *didn't exist yet*. It was *created because* the Stars and Bars was mistaken for the U.S. flag through the smoke at Bull Run — so the game shows the very flag whose confusion started it all. From late 1861 the Eastern Confederate army flies the red **Southern-Cross battle flag**; the Western army around Chickamauga flies the **blue field with a white moon** (the Hardee pattern) — except for the brigades that had just been sent west from Lee's army (Hood's and Kershaw's men), who kept their Eastern battle flags. On the Union side, the **Army of the Potomac corps badges** — the I Corps disc, the II Corps clover (trefoil), the III Corps diamond, the V Corps Maltese cross, the VI Corps Greek cross — now appear as their real shapes, coloured by division (1st red, 2nd white, 3rd blue) and labelled in plain words. And crucially, **the badges only show up at Gettysburg and Chancellorsville** — the badge system wasn't adopted until March 1863, so at the earlier battles the game tells you the corps but notes the badges weren't worn yet. (The earlier version drew the flags as blank coloured rectangles and put the wrong shapes on the badges — all fixed.)

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes how the battle *looks* — a test proves it plays bit-for-bit the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, or your save). The flags are drawn fresh by the game (no image files — it stays a single file), every flag and badge design is sourced to at least two reputable references and fact-checked by a team of AI historians (who confirmed the design and added the Bull-Run and Chickamauga nuances), and a hidden enemy you haven't scouted flies no flag that would give away its position — the fog of war holds. **The bug-hunt — six angles, forty-six AI agents — earned its keep:** it confirmed the new code is clean, drove three improvements (reinforcing brigades now fly proper flags too; a dark-blue badge now reads clearly on the dark panel; a new test locks the no-flag-for-hidden-enemies rule), and *also* uncovered a pre-existing bug in the older battle engine (in the multi-stage battles, the 3D figures aren't rebuilt between stages) — that one is flagged for a separate, dedicated fix since touching it would risk the "plays exactly the same" guarantee. **Verified:** build OK; the new flags test 36/36; the fighting untouched (26/26 byte-identity); the smoke, weather, render, and audio tests all still pass (18/18, 30/30, 30/30, 22/22); the visual test 10/10; Classic still paints; accessibility AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the public-domain photo and reenactment-footage layer — but only with your sign-off first, because it pulls in outside images (and any outside sound files are the same kind of decision). Chattanooga and the USCT battles are still saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-25: **THE BATTLEFIELD FINDS ITS VOICE — turn on the new "Battle ambience" and the field comes alive with sound: the rolling roar of massed musketry, the deep ground-shaking bass of a cannonade, and the bark of each firing brigade coming from exactly where its smoke rises on the field — left, right, near, far — and never from an enemy you can't see**

**Newest (overnight run, D130):** First the battlefield learned to smoke, then to have weather, then to feel alive to the eye — tonight it found its voice. A new **Battle ambience** setting (off until you switch it on) lays a deep, spatial soundscape *under* the existing battle sounds: a continuous **rolling roar of musketry** that swells and ebbs with how hard the fighting is, the **low rumble of a great cannonade** that rises when the guns are really working, and the individual **crack of cannon and rip of musket volleys** placed in stereo exactly where that brigade is on the field — so the sound of the fight comes from where you see the smoke. And just like the smoke, **a brigade you can't see makes no sound that would give away its position** — the fog of war holds for your ears as well as your eyes. It's all generated on the fly (no sound files — the game stays a single file), it reads each battle's intensity live, and there's a one-line caption naming it for anyone using captions.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes how the battle *sounds* — a test proves it plays bit-for-bit the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, or your save; a check even confirms no battle value so much as twitches across 240 audio updates). It's **off by default**, turns itself off entirely for reduced-motion, respects the existing loudness setting (and is kept quieter than the cues it sits beneath, so it's never jarring), and is tuned to stay light on a modest laptop (it caps the number of sounds at once and shuts the whole audio engine down when you leave the battle). **The bug-hunt — six angles, nineteen AI agents — earned its keep:** it caught that the one-time caption could be "used up" before it ever showed (so a player who turned captions on mid-battle would never see it — fixed); that, before your first click, the queued sounds could pile up and all fire at once the instant audio woke (the "stampede" — now they wait for the audio to truly be running); that the sound engine kept idling on the victory screen (now it goes quiet); and a small audio-bookkeeping nit — all four fixed. **Verified:** build OK; the new audio test 22/22; the fighting untouched (26/26 byte-identity); the smoke, weather, and render tests all still pass (18/18, 30/30, 30/30); the visual test 10/10; Classic still paints; the other screens all green. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** fuller flags and corps insignia on the brigades, then — last, and only with your sign-off because it pulls in outside images (and any outside sound files would be the same kind of decision) — the public-domain photo and footage layer. Chattanooga and the USCT battles are still saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **THE BATTLEFIELD ITSELF COMES ALIVE — the ground now has real texture (patches of lush and sun-dried grass, bare trampled earth, the corduroy of a plowed field), the woods sway in the wind, each brigade's colours ripple on the staff, marching columns stride, the brigade you've selected pulses, and a broken brigade fades gently into the ground instead of blinking out — in both the top-down and the 3D views**

**Newest (overnight run, D129):** Last night the battlefield learned to have weather; tonight the field, the trees, and the men themselves came alive. The ground is no longer a flat sheet of green — it grows real **texture**: soft patches of lush and sun-dried grass, the brown of bare trampled earth, and the neat corduroy stripes of a plowed field, all generated procedurally so every battlefield looks like real country. The **woods sway** gently in the wind. Each brigade's **colours ripple** on the staff. A brigade that's actually **marching now strides** with a subtle bob, the one you've **selected pulses** so you never lose it, and when a brigade is **destroyed it fades** softly into the ground over about a second instead of snapping out of existence. It's all there in the simple top-down view and the full 3D battlefield.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes how the battle *looks* — a test proves it plays bit-for-bit the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, or your save; a new test even checks that no brigade's position, strength, or morale so much as twitches while all this is drawn). It turns every bit of motion off for reduced-motion (keeping just the still ground texture), it can be switched off entirely, and it's tuned to stay smooth on a modest laptop (the top-down texture is drawn once and reused, not redrawn every frame). **The bug-hunt — six angles, thirty-seven AI agents — earned its keep and found one real problem:** a destroyed brigade was sinking *far* too fast and too deep, plunging a hundred-plus yards straight through the ground instead of settling gently (the sink was adding up frame after frame). It now settles to a fixed, shallow depth no matter the frame rate. The hunt also caught and fixed seven smaller things — among them, a brigade dying out of your sight could briefly flash into view (a fog-of-war leak, now sealed), and a selected brigade's highlight ring now fades with the body instead of hanging in the air. **Verified:** build OK; the new render test 30/30; the fighting untouched (26/26 byte-identity); the gunsmoke and weather tests still pass (18/18, 30/30); the visual test 10/10 with no graphics warnings; Classic still paints; the other screens all green. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** deeper battle audio (a musketry-and-cannon ambience bed under the existing sound effects, default-off and captioned), then fuller flags, and — last, and only with your sign-off because it pulls in outside images — the public-domain photo and footage layer. Chattanooga and the USCT battles are still saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **EVERY BATTLE NOW HAS ITS OWN SKY — the game gives each fight the weather and light its history records: Antietam opens in the cold dawn fog that filled the Cornfield, the July battles bake in warm afternoon light, the spring battles wake to a cool morning — and where the record calls for it, rain and snow can fall, in both the top-down and the 3D views**

**Newest (overnight run, D128):** Last night the battlefield learned to smoke; tonight it learned to have weather. Each battle now wears the sky its history actually records. **Antietam opens in the pale, cold dawn fog that famously filled the Cornfield** — you can watch the far brigades fade into the mist while the ground in front of you stays clear enough to fight. The summer battles (Gettysburg, Fredericksburg, Malvern Hill, Chickamauga, Bull Run) take on a warm late-afternoon light; the spring mornings (Shiloh, Chancellorsville) wake cool and soft. And the engine can now draw **rain and snow** — drifting streaks and flakes over the field — wherever a battle's record calls for it. A short, spoken-and-printed note names the day's weather as the fight opens.

**Honest about the weather — and wired to nothing in the fighting.** A team of AI historians researched each battle's documented conditions and a second team fact-checked them hard, and the fact-checkers earned their keep: they *refused to invent drama.* Gettysburg's July 3 was bright, not hazy (a college professor's own thermometer-and-sky log proves it); Fredericksburg's famous river fog had lifted before the assault (so the note tells that story, but the sky over the attack is clear and cold); Shiloh's torrential rain fell overnight, *after* the day we model, so the battle itself is fair. The honest lesson it taught: at most of these fights the "fog of war" was *gunsmoke* — which the game already shows — not weather. Only Antietam gets a truly grey, foggy sky. It only changes how a battle *looks* — a test proves it plays bit-for-bit the same as before (it never touches the combat code, the dice, or your save), it turns precipitation off for reduced-motion (keeping just the colour of the sky), it can be switched off entirely, and the fog is always kept thin enough in the distance that you never lose sight of your objective. **The bug-hunt found one real problem and fixed it:** the opening weather note was quietly re-printing itself every single frame (it was keyed to a number that changes constantly during battle) — now it appears exactly once. **Verified:** build OK; the new weather test 30/30; the fighting untouched (26/26 byte-identity); the gunsmoke and the visual tests still pass (18/18, 10/10); Classic still paints; a broad sweep of the other screens all green. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** richer terrain and unit motion — ground texture, a little wind in the trees, rippling banners, and units that move and fall more convincingly. After that: deeper battle audio, fuller flags, and — last, and only with your sign-off because it pulls in outside images — the public-domain photo and footage layer. Chattanooga and the USCT battles are still saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **THE BATTLEFIELD NOW SMOKES — every volley and cannon shot throws up the white black-powder smoke the real war was famous for: it billows from the firing lines, drifts on the wind, gathers into a pall over the hardest-fought ground, and slowly clears — in both the top-down and the 3D views**

**Newest (overnight run, D127):** With all the strategic and teaching work done, the game starts its "make it come to life" pass — and the first thing to come alive is the smoke. In the real Civil War, black-powder muskets and cannon threw up so much white smoke that generals lost sight of their own lines — the smoke *was* the fog of war. Now the game shows it: as your brigades trade fire, gunsmoke rises from the firing lines, the artillery belches a thicker cloud, dust kicks up where rounds strike, and a pall gathers over the worst of the fighting and then drifts off on the wind. It's there in the simple top-down view and in the full 3D battlefield.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes how the battle *looks* — a test proves the battle plays bit-for-bit the same as before (it never touches the combat code, never the dice, never your save). It turns itself completely off for reduced-motion, you can switch it off, it's sized to stay smooth even on a modest laptop, and — importantly — a hidden enemy makes no smoke, so it can never give away a position you haven't scouted. **The bug-hunt (fourteen agents, six angles) came back clean** — only two small things, both fixed: the "hidden enemy makes no smoke" rule had no test guarding it (the rule itself was already right), so a proper test was added; and the smoke dots could in theory draw too large on weak graphics chips, so they're now clamped to what the hardware allows. **Verified:** build OK; the new smoke test 18/18; the fighting untouched (26/26 byte-identity); the visual test 10/10 with no graphics warnings; Classic still paints; a broad sweep of the other screens all green. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** weather and time of day — overcast, rain, fog, and dawn/dusk skies tuned to each battle's real history (a design is already written up). After that: richer terrain and unit motion, deeper battle audio, fuller flags, and — last, and only with your sign-off because it pulls in outside images — the public-domain photo and footage layer. Chattanooga and the USCT battles are still saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **READABLE EVERYWHERE — a top-to-bottom accessibility pass tuned the contrast, labels, focus outlines, and keyboard of every screen in the game (the President's Desk and its tabs, the menus, the live battle, every panel and pop-up) so nothing is too dim to read and everything is reachable without a mouse**

**Newest (overnight run, D126):** This finishes the accessibility work. Every screen got a careful, surface-by-surface check against the professional WCAG 2.2 AA standard, and everything that came up short was fixed at the source. The biggest win: the muted brass label colour and the danger-red used all over the game were just a hair too faint to pass on the dark parchment — both were brightened a touch everywhere at once (the light newspaper-style menu was checked and left exactly as it is). Dozens of small status colours (the green/red "good/bad" readouts on the desk meters, the army-strength and morale lines, the weapon rarity tags) were nudged to fully legible tones; the battle's unit letters got a dark outline so the "U" and "C" read on any uniform colour; and every button, toggle, and expander now announces its state (on/off, expanded/collapsed) and shows a clear focus ring when you Tab to it. Pop-ups now hand keyboard focus back to the button that opened them, and the toast messages are now spoken to screen readers. There's also a built-in **high-contrast boost** that makes the desk and battle panels jump to black-and-bright when you want maximum legibility.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes how the game looks and reads — never how a battle plays (locked by the byte-identity test and the nine battle baselines). **The review was unusually thorough and it paid off:** an automated 28-agent audit found 127 things to fix; a fresh adversarial bug-hunt then caught a subtle trap where a dimmed *row* was quietly fading the very status words we'd just brightened (fixed in three meters), plus a couple of greens that got missed and a focus-handling slip in the battle help pop-up; and two more sweeps after that turned up seven more faint spots (a general's rating word, the rare/common loot tags, a form's error outline, a promotion cost note) — all fixed. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the accessibility test grew to 25/25 with zero page errors; the difficulty test 26/26 (the fighting is untouched); Classic still paints; ~30 screen tests all green. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the strategic-arc work (Phase E) is now complete end to end. The open pillars are more content, the loot-and-survival + play-as-anyone "Soldier's Story" layer, the big graphics/footage/audio "come-to-life" pass, and final polish — with Chattanooga and the USCT battles saved for last.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **PLAY YOUR WAY, SEEN YOUR WAY — a new Accessibility hub lets anyone tune the game to how they read and see: a high-contrast theme, a dyslexia-friendly typeface, colour-blind-safe cues, and screen-reader narration of each turn of the war — reached from a "♿ Accessibility" button on the menu or from the Play Your Way panel**

**Newest (overnight run, D125):** The game now has a one-stop **Accessibility** hub with four modes. **High contrast** brightens the type, borders, and focus outlines and darkens the ground for a sharper read (the parchment newspaper menu, already crisp, is left as it is). **Dyslexia-friendly text** swaps the antique serif for a clean, well-spaced typeface. **Colour-blind safe** turns on the glyphs-and-words cues so which side owns what never depends on colour. **Screen-reader narration** speaks each strategic turn aloud to assistive tech — the battlefield was already narrated, and now the war room is too. There's also a one-click **reduced-motion** switch. Everything is saved and applies everywhere — the menu, the President's Desk, and the battlefield — and the screen reader, keyboard, and focus all work throughout.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** It only changes how the game looks and reads, never how a battle plays (locked by a test that scans the combat code and the nine battle baselines). **This time the full multi-agent bug-hunt DID run** (the servers had recovered) and it earned its keep: it caught a real problem where turning on high contrast made the *main menu* unreadable, and a subtle bug where trying the colour-blind mode could quietly lock you out of turning the colour cues off again — both fixed and locked with tests. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the new accessibility test 17/17 with zero page errors; the difficulty test 26/26 (the fighting is untouched); Classic still paints; the main menu measured a crisp 13.5-to-1 contrast in high-contrast mode; WCAG AA with nothing to fix. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the second half of the accessibility work — a thorough, surface-by-surface WCAG 2.2 AA sweep across every screen (desk tabs, menus, the battle HUD, every panel), auditing and fixing contrast, labels, focus, and keyboard everywhere.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **THE REAL COST — the difficulty dials now teach. Open "What this costs in real life" in the Command & Realism picker and each setting unfolds its history: why heavier casualties, murderous canister, scarce supply, brittle command, and the fog of war cost the men what they did — sourced, honest, and tied to the dial you just moved**

**Newest (overnight run, D124):** The game's difficulty and realism dials no longer just change the battle — they explain it. A new **"What this costs in real life"** panel in the Command & Realism picker unfolds, dial by dial, the real history each setting abstracts: the rifle-musket's terrible arithmetic (Antietam bled some 22,717 men in a single day); canister turning a cannon into a giant shotgun at Malvern Hill; armies that starved when the railroads failed; commands that came apart when a Johnston or a Jackson fell; cavalry as the eyes of the army, and the blindness when Stuart rode out of contact before Gettysburg; green troops becoming veterans in blood; a sharper opponent that decides better but never cheats; and generals fighting half-blind. Each card shows **the setting you've chosen** ("YOURS: HEAVY") and carries its sources. The same teaching now deepens the **Play Your Way** hub's battlefield read-out. It is honest history — slavery named as what the war's cost was borne to end, the Lost Cause given no quarter (Lee's aggression bled the outnumbered South dry), and the "easy" mode marked plainly as a teaching scaffold, not the war. **This completes the whole education layer** — codex, glossary, guided tour, play-style hub, and now the realism teaching.

**Wired to nothing in the fighting.** The whole layer is pure read-out: it reads your settings and shows history, but changes no part of the combat, so every battle plays exactly as before (locked by a test that scans the combat code and the nine battle baselines). **One real bug was caught and fixed:** an early version used a modern regex feature that *older Safari can't even parse* — it would have broken the entire game on those browsers; it's now written in a way every browser understands. (Note for the record: the usual multi-agent bug-hunt couldn't run this time — Anthropic's servers were overloaded — so the review was done directly instead, and it found that bug; a re-run of the full panel is queued for when the servers recover.) **Verified:** build GATE OK; the new test 12/12 with zero page errors; the difficulty test 26/26; Classic still paints; every other test still green; WCAG AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the dedicated accessibility pass — a full WCAG 2.2 AA sweep plus four modes (high-contrast, colour-blind-safe, screen-reader battle narration, and a dyslexia-friendly font).

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **PLAY YOUR WAY — a new hub lets you tell the game how you want to play: lean into running the war as President, into commanding the battles as a General, or both at once — and set how honestly and how unforgivingly it teaches you, from the menu or right from the President's Desk**

**Newest (overnight run, D123):** The game now bends to how *you* want to play it. A new **Play Your Way** hub — reachable from a "⚙ Play Your Way" button on the main menu and from a new **Play Style** tab on the President's Desk — lets you choose a play-style: **President** (you focus on running the war — the economy, the blockade, diplomacy, politics), **General-Commander** (you focus on the battles and your generals), or **Free Command** (both, equally — the way it shipped). It's an emphasis, never a cage: every layer of the war is always one click away whichever you pick, and the choice simply opens the Desk to the part of the war you care about most. Alongside it sits the **Historian's layer** — the teaching and realism settings: show only the alternate history that arises from your own play, jump to the battlefield's difficulty-and-realism controls, or open the display, motion, and sound settings.

**Honest, accessible, and wired to nothing in the fighting.** The whole hub is a pure settings layer: it remembers your preferences but touches no part of the combat, so every battle plays exactly as before. **The bug-hunt (five angles, thirteen agents) found a real one — and it was bigger than the new feature:** the menu's buttons were injected with a one-shot latch, so after you navigated away and came back, the new Play Your Way button **and the existing How-to-Play and Guided Tour buttons** all silently vanished for the rest of the session. All three now re-appear reliably every time you return to the menu. Also fixed: the on/off teaching toggle now announces what it controls to a screen-reader, the menu buttons carry full spoken labels, and a faint divider line was darkened to meet the contrast standard. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the new test 14/14 with zero page errors; Classic still paints; every other test still green; WCAG AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the difficulty and realism sliders — the last piece of the teaching layer.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-24: **A GUIDED TOUR — a new one-minute walkthrough now welcomes you to the whole game: the President's Desk, the battles, the Codex, and the honest paths to victory, all in seven steps you can take by keyboard, mouse, or screen-reader**

**Newest (overnight run, D122):** The game now teaches itself. A new <strong>Guided Tour</strong> &mdash; reachable from the first-launch welcome card, the How-to-Play panel, and a "Guided Tour" button on the main menu &mdash; walks you through all three layers in seven short steps: the war you run from the President's Desk, the great decisions that bend history, the real-time battles your army fights, the Codex and the inline glossary that explain every term, the several honest ways to win, and how to bend the game's difficulty and accessibility to you. Step forward and back with the buttons or the arrow keys, skip anytime, and finish to the field.

**Built for everyone, by design.** The tour is a proper modal dialog: a screen-reader announces each step ("Step 2 of 7: The President's Desk") as it opens, the keyboard focus is trapped inside until you leave, the rest of the page is hidden from assistive tech while it's up, and the whole thing respects reduced-motion. **The bug-hunt (five angles, fourteen agents) found a real accessibility defect and fixed it:** an early version trapped focus in a way that a keyboard user tabbing forward could never reach the "Skip" button &mdash; now the focus cycle is correct in both directions. Also fixed: pressing "?" no longer stacks the help sheet behind the tour, and a few smaller focus and timing rough edges. **The keystone holds &mdash; it's a pure help layer wired to nothing in the fighting**, so every battle plays exactly as before, locked by a test that scans the combat code. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the tutorial test 15/15 with zero page errors; Classic still paints; every other test still green; WCAG AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** play-style presets (President vs General-Commander) and the Historian settings overlay; then the difficulty/realism sliders.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-23: **DEFINITIONS WHERE YOU READ THEM — key terms in the game's teaching text now carry their codex definition: hover, tap, or focus a dotted-underlined term and its meaning appears, drawn from the same sourced encyclopedia**

**Newest (overnight run, D121):** Last night the game gained a sourced encyclopedia — the Codex. Tonight that knowledge comes to where you actually read. In the two richest teaching panels — the graded After-Action report and the "Your War vs History" ledger — key terms now appear with a subtle dotted underline. Hover over one, tap it, or tab to it with the keyboard, and a small card shows its definition, pulled straight from the Codex so there is one source of truth. A screen-reader announces the definition the moment the term receives focus. The terms it knows are the ones the prose actually uses — it understands that "the Lost Cause," "USCT," "Contraband," and "the blockade" are the everyday forms of longer formal names, and links them correctly.

**The keystone — it reads your prose; it never touches the battle.** The glossary is a pure decoration laid over already-rendered teaching text; nothing in the fighting reads it, so every battle plays exactly as before, locked by a test that scans the combat code. **The bug-hunt (five angles, twenty-six agents, run entirely offline) found a real one and fixed it:** an early version of the term-matcher could never recognize any term written with a parenthetical — so "USCT," "the Lost Cause," and a fifth of the glossary would silently never appear. It now derives the plain spoken form of every term, and a strengthened test proves those forms light up. Also fixed: only one term per paragraph used to link (now all of them do), the tap-to-reveal behavior for touch users, and the screen-reader label now leads with exactly what you see. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the glossary test 12/12 with zero page errors; Classic still paints; every other test still green; WCAG AA.

**A note on tonight:** you paused internet access mid-run, so this milestone is **committed locally but not yet pushed** to the remote — it will go up the moment you say resume. (Last night's Codex was already safely pushed.)

**Next:** the guided tutorial, then the play-style presets, then the difficulty/realism sliders.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-23: **THE CODEX — the President's Desk now holds a sourced encyclopedia of the war: its people, its armies, its terms, and the very systems you command — searchable, cross-linked, and honest**

**Newest (overnight run, D120):** With the strategic arc complete, the game turns to teaching. The President's Desk gains a new **Codex** tab — a citation-grade reference of **sixty entries** across four axes: the **people** (Lincoln, Grant, Sherman, Lee, Davis, Forrest, Frederick Douglass, Harriet Tubman, Clara Barton, and more), the **units and formations** (the Army of the Potomac, the Army of Northern Virginia, the United States Colored Troops, the 54th Massachusetts, the Iron and Stonewall brigades), the **terms and concepts** (secession, emancipation, hard war, the Anaconda blockade, King Cotton, Reconstruction, the Lost Cause — named as a myth and refuted), and the **systems of the war** the game itself models. Type to search, filter by axis, and expand any entry to its full teaching prose, its sources, and links to related entries. Every entry is sourced — all sixty carry at least two real citations — and the history is unflinching: slavery is named plainly as the war's cause, the Confederacy is never romanticized, and atrocities are named on both sides, from Fort Pillow to Andersonville to the Union's hard-war burning.

**Researched, fact-checked, and honest.** The entries were written by a team of AI historians and then adversarially fact-checked, and the checkers earned their keep: a non-existent artillery book was caught and removed, and a common error — that Nathan Bedford Forrest *founded* the Ku Klux Klan — was corrected to the truth (he was its first Grand Wizard; it was founded by six Confederate veterans in Pulaski, Tennessee). A second team of twenty-six then tried to break the feature and found only small things, all fixed: a stale caption, a grammar slip, a garbled Lincoln quotation repaired, a dedicated Andersonville entry added for both-sides balance, and the accessibility and tests tightened.

**The keystone — it reads; it never bends the battle.** The Codex is a pure reference wired to nothing in the fighting — no part of the combat engine reads it — so every battle plays exactly as before, now locked by a test that scans the combat code to prove it. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the codex test 18/18 with zero page errors; Classic still paints; every other test still green; WCAG AA. Committed + pushed.

**Next:** the inline glossary — hover or tap a key term anywhere in the game's teaching text and its codex definition appears — then the guided tutorial, the play-style presets, and the difficulty/realism sliders.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-23: **THE WAR CAN END WITHOUT THE LAST BATTLE — break the enemy's will or win Europe's recognition, and the President's desk now offers to conclude the war on those terms, with the full graded report — a negotiated peace or an independence won, not just a chain of battles fought to the end**

**Newest (overnight run, D119):** Until now your war ended only one way: by fighting every battle in the campaign to the last. Tonight it can end the way real wars end — at the negotiating table or by the recognition of foreign powers. When you break the enemy's will to keep fighting (bleed Northern patience to the 1864 election, or shatter the rebellion's resolve), or — as the Confederacy — win a European power's recognition, the President's desk now surfaces an offer between battles: **the war can be concluded.** Accept it, and the war ends then and there with the full graded after-action report — your A-through-F report card, the divergence ledger, the human cost, and the Reconstruction to come — framed for the peace you actually won: *a negotiated peace*, or *a recognized independence*. Or wave it away and fight on for an unconditional victory. The choice, as ever, is yours.

**Honest on every path.** The offer is side-aware and refuses to lie: the Union can never "win" by the South gaining recognition (that would mean the Union is losing), so that path is offered only to the Confederacy — and a Confederate peace is named for exactly what it would have been, the survival of a slaveholding republic, never dressed up as a glorious triumph. The graded report keeps its unflinching accounting whichever way the war ends.

**The keystone — it ends the war, it never bends the battle.** The whole feature is a between-battles offer plus the existing war-end report; nothing in the actual fighting reads any of it, so every battle plays exactly as before, and a war fought to chain's-end still shows the same "The War is Won" screen, byte-for-byte. **The bug-hunt (five angles, ten agents) found three things and all are fixed:** a victory message that said "Northern resolve is breaking" even when you played the Union (whose enemy is the rebellion, not the North); a small state leak that could make the *next* game skip its first strategic turn; and a defensive guard against a stale victory label. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the after-action test 15/15 with zero page errors; Classic still paints; every battle and the divergence/victory tests still green; the new offer banner passes WCAG AA. Committed + pushed. **Phase E's strategic arc — the alternate-history endings and the victory it concludes — is now complete.**

**Next:** the teaching layer — a codex and glossary of the war's people, units, and terms; a guided tutorial; play-style presets; and difficulty/realism sliders.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-23: **THE CHOICES THAT BEND THE WAR — the President's desk now puts four great strategic forks in your hands: how hard to wage the war, on what terms to reunite the country, whether to gamble on King Cotton, and whether to sue for peace or fight on — and each choice steers your war toward one of the alternate endings**

**Newest (overnight run, D118):** Over the last nights the game learned every way your war could end differently — two dozen alternate endings, North and South. Tonight it gives you the wheel. Beside the great Emancipation decision, the President's desk now surfaces **four new "hinge of the war" decision cards**, each a genuine fork at a real turning point, and each one bends your war toward one of those endings. For the Union: **the hard hand of war** (Sherman's march and Sheridan's burning, or a gentler limited war, or Grant's bloody grind — the road to a fast Confederate collapse) and **the terms of reunion** (Lincoln's quick-and-lenient Ten Percent Plan, the radical Wade-Davis program, or forty acres of redistributed land for the freedpeople — the road to a Reconstruction that finally holds). For the Confederacy: **the King Cotton gambit** (embargo the crop to starve Europe's mills, run it through the blockade for gold and guns, or burn it in defiance — the road to recognized independence) and **peace or independence** (send commissioners to Hampton Roads, fight on to break Northern will at the 1864 ballot box, or husband your strength and outlast them — the road to a negotiated peace).

**Real history, honestly told — and no thumb on the scale.** Each card carries the documented record in four voices: a person who was there, the historians who studied it, and — named and then refuted — the Lost Cause myth that grew up around it (that Sherman was a uniquely barbaric butcher; that Reconstruction was a "tragic era" of misrule; that King Cotton was sound strategy betrayed by bad luck; that the South was beaten only by overwhelming numbers). Slavery is named plainly as the war's cause and engine; a Confederate "win" is shown for what it would have been — the survival of a slaveholding republic, never a romantic triumph. Your choices shift the war's momentum, its standing abroad, and its manpower — the very things the endings read — but they never tilt a single battle in your favor.

**The keystone — researched, verified, and hardened.** The card text was written and then adversarially fact-checked by a team of AI historians, and every wobble was fixed: misattributed web links swapped for solid book citations, a contested loan figure softened, a famous Senate quotation restored to its exact words. A second team of nine then tried to break it and found nothing real to fix. **Verified:** build GATE OK; the decisions test 19/19 with zero page errors; the desk still renders; Classic still paints; no battle code touched. And the accessibility pass caught a bonus — two old contrast problems in the decision cards (there since the system was built) are now fixed for everyone. Committed + pushed. **Phase E's alternate-history pillar is now substantially complete.**

**Next:** wiring a reached ending to a real war-ending screen, so a negotiated peace or a recognized independence actually ends your war with the graded report; then the codex, tutorial, and play-style presets; then the full accessibility pass.
