# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-21: **CHICKAMAUGA — the river of death** (the 3-phase Western epic: the woods → Longstreet's breakthrough → Thomas's stand; probe 18/18, pushed)

**Newest:** Chickamauga is playable and verified — the bloodiest battle of the Western theater, fought as three sectors in sequence. A new **⚔ BATTLE — CHICKAMAUGA (1863)** main-menu button opens the side-choice card; command the army of your choosing. **Sep 19, the woods:** a blind, confused meeting engagement in dense timber where neither side can see — the Union line holds the road into the night. **Sep 20, Longstreet's breakthrough:** a Union staff error pulls Wood's division out of line at the Brotherton farm at the exact moment Longstreet's deep column happens to strike that point; the Union right and center collapse and stream toward Chattanooga. **Sep 20 afternoon, the Rock of Chickamauga:** George Thomas rallies the survivors on Snodgrass Hill and Horseshoe Ridge and holds until dark — reinforced by Granger and Steedman marching unordered to the sound of the guns — saving the Army of the Cumberland from destruction. The Confederates win the field, but at a fearful cost they cannot afford, and Bragg fails to pursue: the victory is squandered into the siege of Chattanooga and the November reversal.

It is the **fourth multi-phase epic** on the T8 engine (after Antietam, Gettysburg, Vicksburg), built as a data file + one registry line — no new combat code. **Top-level attacker = CS / defender = US** across all three phases (the Army of the Cumberland fought on the defensive), so the CS player is the offensive (Bragg/Longstreet) and the US player holds (Thomas). The teaching is **contingency over genius** (the breakthrough was a chain of accidents, not Confederate martial superiority) and **the squandered victory**; the "River of Death" name is shipped only as the disputed legend it is. One universal combat model, **no per-battle damage fudge** — outcomes emerge from the historical OOB, terrain, timing, and tactics.

**Balance (AI-vs-AI, 32 seeds, deterministic):** the woods hold for the Union 32/32 (a mutual bloodbath); Longstreet's breakthrough carries 32/32 (the decisive, triple-weighted phase, the US routed cheaply); Thomas's ridge holds 32/32 with the Confederate assault paying about 3-to-1 (the failed-assault lesson); **aggregate Confederate tactical victory 32/32** — and a human Union player who closes the Wood gap **overturns** the battle. The army that won the field **bled more** in the aggregate — the costly-victory teaching, now locked by a probe assertion.

**Bug-hunt (10 Opus agents): 2 confirmed + 3 critic gaps, all fixed.** The standout (the same class the Vicksburg hunt caught): **Charles Harker was a COLONEL at Chickamauga, not a "Brig. Gen."** — his brigadier-generalcy was dated to the battle but came afterward, exactly like Hans Heg, whom the data already gets right. Corrected, plus four probe-rigor guards (per-phase casualty direction, the phase winners, and the aggregate "the winner bled more" lesson).

**Verified:** build GATE OK; `probe-chickamauga` **18/18**, 0 pe; full no-regression GREEN (every battle baseline byte-identical + the tactical-systems suite + custom-builder 9/9 + tactical-visuals now capturing live Chickamauga 2D/3D, texWarn 0; diag-classic nonBlank 346; boot/t1 ok; 0 pageerrors); WCAG inherited-AA (no new color). Pushed to `adhanke-star/History-Video-Game` main (D90).

**Next:** **Chattanooga** — the Union reversal (Orchard Knob → Lookout Mountain "Battle Above the Clouds" → Missionary Ridge), built from the design brief at `.tmp/chattanooga-design.md`; then the **C3 USCT battles** (the Crater · New Market Heights · Olustee · Nashville).

---

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-21: **ENGINEERING CORPS — PONTOON BRIDGING** (the pontoon train; increment 3 of 3 → THE CORPS IS COMPLETE; probe 22/22, player-only/byte-identical)

**Newest:** the Engineering Corps is finished — all three of Aaron's locked "all of the above" (entrench + abatis + pontoons). A new **opt-in river** actually blocks movement: you cross it at a **shallow ford** (slow), a **deep ford** (only fordable at Arcade realism — otherwise you must bridge it), or a **pontoon bridge** you lay with an infantry brigade on the near bank (key **N**, or the "Pontoon" button), which takes time and then opens a fast crossing. Try it from **Skirmish → Ground → "River crossing."** The **realism slider** decides how fast the engineers work, how slow the fords are, and whether a deep crossing needs a pontoon at all; a strong strategic Engineer Works Corps lays bridges faster in a campaign battle. It is rendered as a slate-blue river with boat-and-plank pontoons and stepping-stone fords (CVD-safe, reduceMotion-safe) in 2D, and a water plane with floating pontoon boats in 3D, with a sourced teaching card on the Fredericksburg pontoon delay (laid under Barksdale's fire) and Grant's ~2,100-ft James River bridge of 1864.

This is **increment 3** (the last), still all in `src/tactical/T13-engineering.js`. It is a **player tool** (the AI never lays pontoons or paths to fords), so every AI-vs-AI baseline is byte-for-byte unchanged; a river skirmish frames you as the attacker forcing the crossing while the AI defends the far bank. Bull Run's creek/Stone Bridge stay cosmetic (making them live would regress a shipped battle) — the teaching card cites the Rappahannock as the historical anchor.

**Bug-hunt (19 agents): 8 confirmed + 6 critic gaps, all fixed.** The big ones: a unit standing on a ford could **sidestep into deep water and wade across** (closed — you can only enter the water from a crossing, but a unit shoved in can still crawl out); the **3D water was buried under the ground** and invisible (raised to a thin sheet on the surface); and a brigade ordered across impassable water would **march in place forever and exhaust itself** (now it halts at the bank and tells you why). The river skirmish was also rebalanced so it works for either side you pick.

**Verified:** build GATE OK; `probe-engineering-corps` **22/22**; full no-regression **GREEN (21 probes byte-identical, 0 pageerrors, diag-classic `nonBlank:346`)**; WCAG-AA on all new UI; the help overlay now lists the B/X/N engineering keys. Pushed to `adhanke-star/History-Video-Game` main (D89).

**Next:** the Engineering Corps is complete → Phase C tactical breadth — **Chickamauga / Chattanooga**, then the **C3 USCT battles**.

---

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-21: **ENGINEERING CORPS — ABATIS / OBSTACLES** (the axe; increment 2 of "all of the above"; probe 15/15, player-only/byte-identical)

**Newest:** the Engineering Corps grows a second tool. A selected player infantry brigade can now build an **abatis** — felled timber with sharpened branches laid across its front (key **B**, or the in-battle "Abatis" button). Enemy troops forcing the belt are **slowed**, **disordered** once per crossing (a morale + fatigue hit that makes their next volleys ragged), and recover after a few seconds; a nearby brigade **clears** a lane through it (key **X**). It is *not* a magic wall — the game models friction (slow + disorder + deliberate clearing), not extra casualties from the timber. Build time, clear time, the slow, and the disorder all **read the B-5 realism slider** (Historian bites harder and works slower than Arcade). Rendered as a 2D stake-line + 3D crossed timber (fog-gated), with a Mahan-sourced teaching card.

This is **increment 2** of Aaron's locked "all of the above" corps (entrench + abatis + pontoons), still all in `src/tactical/T13-engineering.js`. It is a **player tool** (no AI builds), so every AI-vs-AI baseline is byte-for-byte unchanged. The abatis code was authored 2026-06-20 but was left uncommitted/unvetted when the prior **Codex** session ran out of usage (Codex's only landed work was the browser-probe Seatbelt guard, committed separately); this session brought it through the full vetting gate + bug-hunt and pushed it.

**Bug-hunt (16 agents): 8 confirmed + 4 critic gaps, all fixed.** The big one (**HIGH**): abatis belts were **leaking across phases** in multi-phase battles (Vicksburg/Antietam/Gettysburg) — a phase-1 belt kept slowing/disordering phase-2 enemies at stale map coordinates. Fixed with a per-phase reset that drops the belts but keeps the teaching flag. Also fixed: abandoned belts now decay (they were permanently eating the 4-belt cap), the render now respects fog-of-war, ids no longer collide on the same tick, and routing units are no longer morale-docked by the belt. Kept as correct: an entrenched line *with* an abatis apron (Fredericksburg/Cold Harbor) and one disorder shock per crossing.

**Verified:** build GATE OK; `probe-engineering-corps` **15/15**; full no-regression **GREEN (50 probes, 0 pageerrors, diag-classic `nonBlank:346`)**. Fixed a stale D86 probe along the way (`probe-custom-battle-builder` had omitted Vicksburg from its registry baseline → 9/9). Commits `679ee7d` (Codex guard + repo hygiene) → `02b2dd8` (abatis, **D88**), pushed to `adhanke-star/History-Video-Game` main.

**Next (the LAST engineering increment):** **PONTOON bridging** — a new river/water terrain feature + bridge-laying + a crossing gate (fordable vs requires-pontoon, realism-gated). That completes the corps; then on to C tactical breadth (Chickamauga/Chattanooga, C3 USCT).

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-20: **ENGINEERING CORPS — FIELD ENTRENCHMENTS** (the spade; increment 1 of "all of the above"; probe 8/8, byte-identical)

**Newest:** the Tactical Engineering Corps has begun. A player brigade can now **Entrench** (key **E**, or the in-battle "Entrench" button) — it digs in where it stands and, over ~70 sim-seconds, earns parapet-grade **cover** (the war's drift toward trench warfare). Marching off the works abandons them. The dig **reads the B-5 realism slider**: Arcade digs fast for modest cover (×1.43), Historian slow for strong cover (×1.81), Balanced ×1.62. The parapet is **facing-aware** — it shelters the front, so a flank/rear maneuver still beats fixed works. Rendered as a 2D dirt parapet + a 3D dirt berm (low-tier aware, reduceMotion-safe).

Aaron locked the full corps ("**all of the above**" — entrench + abatis + pontoons), so this is **increment 1**; it ships as `src/tactical/T13-engineering.js` (architected to host the other two). Built as 9 guarded byte-identical T0 seams + `tools/probe-engineering-corps.mjs` (8/8). Entrenchment is a **player tool** in this increment (no scenario/AI digs), so every AI-vs-AI baseline is byte-for-byte unchanged.

**Bug-hunt (17 agents):** 1 confirmed — the cover was omnidirectional; fixed to be facing-aware (front full / flank half / rear none) so flanking counters works. Critics triaged (melee charger-exposed is the correct base convention; the multi-phase 3D works self-heal; the fog-ghost-works case is deferred to when AI/scenario entrenchment lands).

**Verified:** build GATE OK; probe-engineering-corps 8/8; full no-regression suite byte-identical (field/bullrun/shiloh/fog/ai/autopause + all battle probes + officers/logistics/arms/presets/csplayer/campaign-link); tactical-visuals 8/8 (`textureWarnings:0`); diag-classic `nonBlank:346`; boot/t1 ok; 0 pageerrors. (D87.)

**Next (the rest of the corps):** ABATIS / obstacles, then PONTOON bridging (needs a new river terrain feature) — each its own vetted increment extending T13. See the T13 module header for the EXTENSION POINTS.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-20: **VICKSBURG — THE 3-PHASE RIVER-FORTRESS SIEGE** (the last Codex project, finished + adversarially hardened; probe 18/18)

**Newest:** Vicksburg is now playable and verified — the first SIEGE in the game, built as a three-phase battle on the T8 multi-phase engine: **the Stockade Redan (May 19) → the Forlorn Hope at the Great Redoubt (May 22) → the Saps and the Mine against the 3rd Louisiana Redan (June 25)**. A new **⚔ BATTLE — VICKSBURG (1863)** main-menu button opens the side-choice card; command Grant's besiegers or Pemberton's garrison across all three sectors, the cost carrying forward, and the end-screen scores the siege phase-by-phase with the Mississippi split and the city's fall. Anti-Lost-Cause throughout: Vicksburg is *dug out*, not merely starved out.

**This was the last uncompleted Codex project** (left dirty in the working tree). It was brought through the full PROPER VETTING gate AND an adversarial bug-hunt (25 agents) that found real defects — every one fixed:
- **History:** Louis Hebert was misattributed to the Stockade Redan (and stamped "Verified"). That northern sector was **M.L. Smith's division**; Hebert held the **3rd Louisiana Redan** under Forney. Corrected and given honest provenance.
- **Teaching/balance:** the failed May assaults were INVERTED — the dug-in defender bled more than the exposed attacker (the opposite of the cards, and of the Fredericksburg lesson). Rebalanced toward fire parity + the fortress's historical gun edge, so **the May assaults now cost the attacker (US:CS 1.93 and 2.64), the redans still hold 8/8, the siege still wins 8/8, and Vicksburg falls 8/8** with a clear score margin (US 3 / CS 2). A new casualty-direction probe gate locks this so it can never silently re-invert.
- **T12 readability:** fixed a GPU leak (per-sync SpriteMaterials + selection meshes never disposed), gated the selection halo on the low GPU tier, and put the strength count on a fixed dark pill for WCAG-AA contrast.

**Verified:** build GATE OK; `probe-vicksburg` 18/18, 0 pe; `probe-tactical-roster` 8/8 (now guards 8 battles); bullrun 15/15; malvern-hill 24/24; antietam 16/16; fredericksburg 22/22; chancellorsville 24/24; gettysburg 16/16; shiloh 29/29; field/officers/logistics/arms/presets/csplayer/campaign-link all green; `probe-tactical-visuals` 8/8 with `textureWarnings:0`; bootprobe ok (10 tolerated 404s); t1probe ok; diag-classic paints (`nonBlank:346`); `git diff --check` clean. The sim engine T0–T8 was untouched. (D86.)

**Next priority (non-battle):** the **Tactical Engineering Corps** on the field — pontoons, entrenchments, abatis, obstacle-clearing — interacting with the B-5 difficulty/realism sliders (Aaron's run-k directive, V1-CHECKLIST Phase F + B-5 pointer). Other open Codex-owned items: C3 USCT battles, S3 alt-history, S4 codex/glossary, the comprehensive WCAG pass, the full-campaign playthrough probe.

# ☀ WAKE-UP — 2026-06-18: **CUSTOM BATTLE BUILDER C4 COMPLETE** (single-phase tactical scenario authoring; import/export/slots/launch gates green)

**Newest:** C4 is now playable and verified. The main menu has a first-class **Custom Battle Builder** flow for real-time tactical scenarios: scenario metadata, sides/briefs, objective, field size, terrain hills/woods/walls/markers, OOB units, artillery/gun counts, reinforcement/deployment timing, optional leaders, supply, teaching cards, provenance, export/shareable JSON, import, and six local persistence slots.

**Architecture:** C4 is intentionally **single-phase V1**. Phase authoring is deferred until an editor for `phases[]` can be probed as safely as authored historical phases. Custom scenarios stay out of the historical `fldScenarioRegistry()`; `fldScenarioData(id)` falls back to `fldCustomScenarioData(id)` only for explicit `custom_...` IDs. Valid customs launch through the same single-phase `fldScenarioInit` path as historical battles, with field size reset every launch before custom `field.w/h` is applied.

**Validation:** required fields, safe unique IDs, unsafe JSON keys, duplicate IDs, bounds/clamps, objective placement, reinforcement timing, side ownership, leader attachment ownership, realistic artillery crew ratios (12-40 per gun), malformed JSON, `phases[]`, and forbidden combat/damage keys are all blocked. Custom artillery uses the universal gun model; no per-battle damage fudge was added.

**Verified:** `node tools/build.mjs` GATE OK; `node tools/probe-custom-battle-builder.mjs` 9/9; `node tools/probe-tactical-roster.mjs` 8/8; `node tools/probe-field.mjs` 13/13; `node tools/probe-bullrun.mjs` 15/15; `node tools/probe-malvern-hill.mjs` 24/24; `node tools/probe-antietam.mjs` 16/16; `node tools/probe-fredericksburg.mjs` 22/22; `node tools/probe-chancellorsville.mjs` 24/24; `node tools/probe-gettysburg.mjs` 16/16; `node tools/probe-shiloh.mjs` 29/29; officers/logistics/arms/presets/csplayer/campaign-link probes all green; `node tools/probe-tactical-visuals.mjs` 6/6; boot/t1 ok; Classic diag nonBlank 346; `git diff --check` clean. # ☀ WAKE-UP — run k (2026-06-16): **PHASE C-1 — FREDERICKSBURG SHIPPED** (the Marye's-Heights slaughter is now playable: storm the open glacis as the Union, or hold the stone wall for the Confederacy as charge after charge breaks before it — and the tactical engine is now data-driven, so each new battle is just a data file)

**⚔ NEWEST (this firing) — PHASE C-1 · FREDERICKSBURG (the Assault on Marye's Heights):** the SECOND real-time battle, and the start of Phase C (tactical breadth). A new **⚔ Battle — Fredericksburg (1862)** button on the main menu opens a side-choice card: **lead the Union assault** (form in the town, cross the canal, and storm the open glacis toward the sunken Telegraph Road — try to do what the Army of the Potomac could not) or **hold for the Confederacy** behind the four-foot stone wall, the pre-sighted guns on Marye's Heights raking the field, as charge after charge breaks before you. The big change under the hood: the engine is now **battle-agnostic** — Fredericksburg added zero new combat code; it is a data file (`data/fredericksburg.json`) plus one registry line, with all the menu/side-choice/briefing/end-screen text now read from the data. Adding Antietam or Gettysburg next is the same recipe.

**The historical fidelity took a real mechanic.** The attacker AI built in Phase B is *good* — left to itself it concentrates and rushes home the bayonet, which is exactly what Fredericksburg's assault was NOT. So this battle declares its AI attacker "doomed": it advances in line across the open ground and trades fire, but it never makes the cheap column-rush or the mass bayonet charge — Burnside's piecemeal disaster. The result is the historical slaughter: the assault is **denied 8 times out of 8**, the Union pays **nearly twice** the Confederate cost, and none of it touches Bull Run (the flag is off everywhere else, byte-for-byte). Unlike Bull Run, Fredericksburg fights in **clear weather** (the morning fog had lifted — "a chicken could not live on that field"); the defense wins on the stone wall's cover and the massed crest canister instead of fog. A *human* commanding the Union is unbound by the "doomed" flag — the alt-history door is open if you can do what the real army could not.

**The bug-hunt earned its keep — it caught the balance's heart.** An empirical trace found that the defending line was *marching off the stone wall* on the first second of the fight (the defender AI aims for the objective's forward edge, which I'd placed in front of the wall) — so the wall's cover was going unused and the whole "killing machine" was really just the guns. Fixed by seating the objective the way Bull Run does, so the holding line lands exactly on the wall in cover while the attacker dies exposed a few yards out; a new live-position check makes sure it can't regress. **Measured:** Confederate **8/8**, Union casualties **≈1.91×** the Confederate, the wall load-bearing, the line provably holding the wall in cover. **probe-fredericksburg 20/20**; all eleven existing tactical baselines stayed **byte-identical** (Bull Run still 15/15, command-either-side still 16/16); bootprobe ok; t1probe 14/14; diag-classic 346; 0 page-errors; WCAG-AA clean (the new UI reuses already-audited parts). Single file ≈**1.74 MB**. Committed + pushed (DECISIONS **D73**). **Next up (DECISIONS D74, Aaron-locked): ANTIETAM as a MULTI-PHASE battle** (the Cornfield → the Sunken Road → Burnside's Bridge), which means first building a sequential-phase engine capability. The guiding rule Aaron set: the combat model stays ONE consistent ruleset across every battle (a rifle/cannon does the same damage everywhere) — outcomes come from the historical scenario design and the tactics each side uses, not per-battle fudging; so the first cleanup is to replace Fredericksburg's inflated artillery "proxy men" with a consistent gun-model and re-tune by geometry. New battles stay standalone menu entries for now.

**The old B-6 summary follows below.**

**⚔ (prior firing) — PHASE B-6 · CS-PLAYER "COMMAND EITHER SIDE":** the real-time battles can now be fought from EITHER army. The **⚔ First Bull Run** button opens a **side-choice card** — *Lead the Union* (the historical assault: cross Bull Run, storm Henry House Hill before the trains arrive) or **Hold for the Confederacy** (stand on the hill and deny it to McDowell's army while the rail-borne reserves come up). Choose the Confederacy and you DEFEND — and the **B-1 attacker AI** is now pointed at *you*, massing on a flank and pressing the bayonet, which is exactly what makes that whole attacker doctrine finally player-facing. The Skirmish side pick is fully wired too, and a Confederate campaign commands the Confederate army in its battles. Everything follows the side you took: the field renders from your end (the 3D camera sits behind your own line), the fog shows only what *your* scouts see, the briefing states *your* task (seize-and-hold vs hold-and-deny), the HUD names your army ("4 Confederate vs 1 Union"), and the end screen teaches from the side you played. **This completes Phase B — the full tactical-depth arc (smarter AI · officers · logistics · arm roles · difficulty presets · command-either-side).**

**The bug-hunt earned its keep (52 agents) — and so did vetting before it.** Vetting first caught a regression I'd introduced: commanding the Confederates *in a campaign* briefly showed the wrong army's officers/fog (the side-resolver trusted a stale value) — fixed so a Confederate campaign is read live. Then the hunt's headline catch: hitting **"Fight Again"** after a custom skirmish as the Confederacy used to drop you into the generic Union sandbox with **no units you could command** — now the rematch replays your exact battle (and the sandbox itself honors your side). It also pointed the 3D camera behind *your* line (you were looking from behind the enemy), and — a teaching-integrity fix — stopped fog-hidden enemy reinforcements from being announced/banner'd/auto-paused, so you only learn of the enemy's reserves when you actually scout them.

**Measured:** **byte-identical for the Union default** (every existing launch resolves exactly as before — the 10 tactical baselines stayed byte-identical, the live Bull Run is still Confederate **8/8** under fog, B-6 moved nothing); the **Confederate defense is winnable** (the role-aware defender holds the hill 8/8 under fog — a human can match it); the fog render provably hides the enemy from *your* viewer and never your own men. **probe-csplayer 16/16**, 0 page-errors; t1probe 14/14; diag-classic 346; WCAG-AA clean (2 contrast fixes). Single file ≈**1.70 MB**. Committed + pushed (DECISIONS **D72**). **Next up: Phase C — tactical BREADTH** (the Eastern marquee first: Antietam, Fredericksburg, Gettysburg, Chancellorsville on the now-mature engine). *(Also reviewed an outside "how to build this for $0" report — D71 — and kept our own engine/art/tooling choices, which fit this project better; a few publishing notes were filed for later.)*

**The old B-5 summary follows below.**

**⚙ (prior firing) — PHASE B-5 · DIFFICULTY & REALISM PRESETS:** every real-time battle can now be tuned to you. A new **"⚙ Command & Realism"** screen (main menu, and from the Skirmish setup) sets **two dials**: the **AI level** — Recruit · Regular · Veteran · Hardee — and the **realism** — Arcade · Balanced · Historian — with an **"Advanced"** drawer that exposes every individual lever (casualty severity, canister lethality, supply strictness, command-shock, scouting range, experience weight, AI sharpness, fog, auto-pause). The promise it keeps: **the AI never cheats.** Harder doesn't hand the enemy extra strength — it makes the enemy *decide sharper* (commit the assault and counterattack on tighter judgment, the B-1 doctrine). The single hand-up — a steadier-troops cushion plus a greener enemy — appears **only at the easiest tier (Recruit)**, and it's stated plainly on the card. **"Balanced" is exactly today's shipped battle** (the historically-tuned numbers, First Bull Run under fog), and choosing it changes nothing — it reproduces the current result seed-for-seed. **Arcade** is the forgiving on-ramp (lighter casualties, generous supply, gentle command shock, fog off); **Historian** is the unforgiving real thing (heavier attrition, strict supply, murderous canister, hard command shock, fog on). In any battle, the control bar's **"⚙ Settings"** (key **G**) opens a quick drawer for live fog/auto-pause/speed. Pick **Recruit × Arcade** to learn the maneuvers; **Hardee × Historian** to feel the real cost. *(The tactical Engineering Corps — pontoons, entrenchments, abatis — is its own later milestone; B-5 lays the sliders it will read.)*

**The bug-hunt earned its keep (76 agents).** It caught a genuinely nasty one: pressing **Escape to close the in-battle settings drawer used to tear down the whole battle** (the key bubbled through to the exit handler) — now the drawer owns the keyboard while it's open. It also hardened the difficulty system against a corrupted/hand-edited saved preset (a bad value can no longer zero out casualties into a never-ending battle, flip a lever backwards, or secretly buff the AI — the enemy-resolve ceiling is now enforced in code, not just data), fixed the picker's keyboard semantics, and stopped a "let the battle decide the fog" preset from quietly overriding your in-battle **V** toggle. All 13 confirmed findings + 6 critic gaps fixed and re-tested.

**Measured:** **Balanced == today, byte-identical** — the 8-seed Bull Run AI-vs-AI is Confederate **8/8** with no preset and with an explicit Veteran×Balanced, seed-for-seed; Arcade vs Historian produce measurably different battles; the AI ladder is monotonic and the cushion is Recruit-only. **probe-presets 26/26**; all nine existing tactical baselines stayed **byte-identical**; WCAG-AA clean (3 contrast fixes); deterministic. Single file ≈**1.68 MB**. Committed + pushed (DECISIONS **D70**). **Next up: B-6 — command EITHER side** (defend as the Confederates while the B-1 attacker AI presses you).

**The old B-4 summary follows below.**

**⚔ (prior firing) — PHASE B-4 · DISTINCT ARM ROLES on the tactical field:** the batteries and horsemen now fight as themselves. **Artillery** delivers **canister** at close range — a giant shotgun that flays a line in the open but is blunted by stone walls and woods — and a slower long-range bombardment beyond; a battery is **overrun if you let infantry reach it**, and the doctrine is asymmetric: a defending battery sits sited-safe and limbers away early, while an *attacking* battery is pushed forward to deliver canister and can be caught (Griffin's and Ricketts's guns on Henry House Hill, whose loss broke the Union attack). **Cavalry** runs four roles — **scout** (riding wide to lift the fog), **screen** (denying the enemy his eyes), **flank** (the open wing and the saber charge — shock that shatters a wavering line but breaks on a braced one), and **raid** (making for the enemy's ammunition trains to drain them). And the **Cannon Corps you buy on the President's Desk now becomes the battery you field** — a Napoleon park gives murderous canister, a Whitworth park a long-range counter-battery with no close punch.

**Two things the vetting earned.** (1) A real **byte-identity bug the design had missed**: the frozen base engine already defined the arm melee table (a battery melees at 0.40, cavalry at 1.05), and my first refactor had quietly dropped those to 1.0 — caught by diffing against the committed build and fixed (the off-state now reads the base table exactly). (2) A **balance fork I surfaced to you**: because each tactical layer's test turns the others off, the *stacked* config (officers + logistics + arms) had never been measured — and in clear weather it makes the AI-vs-AI Bull Run Union-favored (a problem that was already present before this milestone). Fog-on it's solidly Confederate (the hill holds). **Your call: First Bull Run now opens under fog** — the historically faithful battle of smoke and broken ground, where fog aids the defender and the Confederates hold Henry House Hill (press **V** to clear the weather). The whole live config now resolves Confederate-favored, as history did.

**The old B-3 summary follows below.**

**⚔ (prior firing) — PHASE B-3 · IN-BATTLE LOGISTICS on the tactical field:** the real-time battle gains an **ammunition economy**. Each side now fields a rear **ammunition train** with a finite battle reserve; a brigade that breaks off the firing line and reaches its train **refills its cartridge boxes** (drawing the reserve down), and when the reserve runs dry the army "runs low" — the real decider behind the 20th Maine's bayonet charge at Little Round Top. A brigade out of cartridges while holding the contested ground **fires dry, then goes to the bayonet** rather than abandoning the hill; a brigade pushed past exhaustion can barely drag itself forward. The **attacker's train sits far behind its start line** (it outruns its supply — Clausewitz's culminating point) and the **defender's just behind the objective it holds**, and the whole reserve **scales with the supply you built on the President's Desk** (a raid order cuts the enemy's) — so the logistics you win strategically pay off on the field.

**The bug-hunt earned its keep — and turned up a teaching-breaker.** A 64-agent adversarial hunt found that with **Fog of War on**, the new ammunition economy *inverted* one of the game's core lessons — "fog aids the defender" (the Henry House Hill lesson). At First Bull Run with fog on, the Confederate defender went from winning every AI-vs-AI game to *losing* every one: under fog the battle becomes a long fire-trade, and the attacker could cycle fresh, resupplied brigades to its safe rear train and simply out-shoot the pinned defender. Because it **contradicted a shipped teaching, I stopped and surfaced it to you** rather than silently patching it. Your first instinct (let the defender refill on its own depot) turned out to do nothing — the defender wasn't the side running dry — so we went with the fix that works: **an attacker advancing blind can't run its trains forward, so it fights with what it carries.** The result is clean: logistics is now **balance-neutral with fog either way** (Confederate 5/8 fog-off, 8/8 fog-on — each matching the no-logistics baseline), and a regression-guard test locks the fog case so it can never silently re-invert.

**Measured (8-seed Bull Run AI-vs-AI, Confederate=defender win count):** fog-off 5/8 with or without logistics (neutral); fog-on 8/8 with or without logistics (fog still aids the defender). **probe-logistics 14/14**; all seven existing tactical baselines stayed **byte-identical** (the layer is provably the only change); WCAG-AA clean (one HUD-contrast nudge). Single file ≈**1.61 MB**. Committed + pushed (DECISIONS **D66**). **Next up: B-4 distinct arm roles** — real artillery (canister up close, long-range out far) and cavalry (scout / flank / screen / raid) — already designed and ready to build.

---

**◀ Previously — PHASE B-2 · OFFICERS & COMMAND on the tactical field:** leadership now lives on the real-time battlefield. Named field leaders ride with their army and project a **command radius** — brigades inside it recover morale faster, hold longer before they break, and rally from a rout sooner (the historical job of a general: rallying the line in person). And they **can be hit** — a commander who rides too long within musket range of the firing line is wounded, then falls; his command aura dies and the troops around him take a morale shock (the "the general is down!" rout trigger). At First Bull Run you watch the real command cast: McDowell and Heintzelman driving the Union assault; Beauregard, Johnston, and — on Henry House Hill — Bee, Bartow, and (arriving by rail at 135s) Jackson. It **ties the generals you appoint on the President's Desk** (S2 m5): in a campaign battle your appointed commander's leadership rating sets his field quality, and his name rides the field.

**The bug-hunt earned its keep.** The first cut killed generals far too easily — the Confederate commanders who *survived* First Bull Run were dying in nearly every game, which a teaching wargame must never assert as fact. A 52-agent adversarial hunt caught it (and seven more), and the fix is now history-honest: a per-leader **historical durability** (Bee and Bartow, the real casualties, are fall-prone; the army commanders endure), accumulated risk that **decays when a general withdraws to safety**, and **cover** that shelters a commander on the reverse slope — so Jackson's stand is rewarded by position, not luck. Army commanders now survive **10 of 10** test battles; a general falling is a rare, dramatic hinge, not background noise.

**Measured (officers ON, 8-seed Bull Run AI-vs-AI, Confederate=defender win count):** the dense Confederate command on Henry House Hill (5 leaders to the Union's 2) lifts the defender from **5/8 to 7/8** fog-OFF (the historical command stand — yet the Union attacker still breaks through 1/8) and **8/8 fog-ON** (fog still aids the defender; no regression from B-1). probe-officers **15/15**; the six existing tactical baselines stayed byte-identical; the false-death banner cascade is gone.

---

**◀ Previously — PHASE B-1 · the smarter DEFENDER-FAVORED ATTACKER AI:** the complement to the Confederate-defender doctrine. Until now the tactical attacker AI just advanced and traded fire at range — which a defender in cover always wins — so it could never crack a defended hill (AI-vs-AI Bull Run was a Union walkover only because the *defender* was passive; once the defender got smart, the attacker had no answer). Now the attacker **concentrates on the weaker flank, closes, and presses the bayonet home** (melee + numbers beat fire + cover). Two locks you set (charter fork #2): it commits **gradually** (massing unit by unit, not flipping the whole army at once), and **fog aids the defender** — under fog the attacker won't blind-assault a hill whose reserves it can't see; it advances cautiously and gets mauled by the concealed brigades, exactly as at Henry House Hill in 1861.

**Measured (8-seed A/B, Bull Run AI-vs-AI, Confederate=defender win count):** old passive attacker → CS **2/8** fog-OFF (a Union sweep). New attacker → CS **6/8** fog-OFF (still Confederate-favored and historical, but now **competitive — the Union breaks through 2/8**) and **8/8 fog-ON** (fog robustly aids the defender — the prototype's fog *inversion* is tuned out). And it's a real fight now: defender casualties **4592** vs the old passive attacker's 1276 (~3.6× bloodier). The human-Union player remains the primary mode (you *are* the attacker there and out-play the AI); AI-vs-AI is the diagnostic, and a Confederate-favored AI duel is the faithful result.

**Quality:** adversarial bug-hunt (4 lenses, Opus) → 2 findings, both fixed — the important one: a lone visible picket could "unblind" the attacker into assaulting the hidden mass behind it (it broke the fog lock), so the fog caution now gates **directly on fog**, not on what's currently sighted (strictly safer). **probe-ai 15/15**; tactical no-regression GREEN (sandbox/Bull-Run/fog/auto-pause all held, Classic still paints); 0 pageerrors. Single file ≈1.55 MB. Committed + pushed (DECISIONS **D64**).

---

**⚔ PREVIOUS (this run) — PHASE A · CONNECT THE TWO LAYERS:** the strategic army now fields in the real-time fight, and the fight feeds the war.

**⚔ NEWEST (this firing) — PHASE A · CONNECT THE TWO LAYERS (the first V1-CHECKLIST item, D61→D62):** until now "The Civil War" was two separate games bolted together — an owner-mode grand-strategy **desk** (run the economy, raise corps, appoint generals) and a real-time **tactical engine** (the sandbox + First Bull Run), with no wire between them. **Phase A is that wire.** The army your *whole war* built — manpower, the weapons you bought, your generals, morale — now actually **takes the field** in the real-time fight, and the result of that fight flows **back** into the campaign. Three ties:
- **A1 — your war conditions the battle.** When you fight a campaign battle in real time, your brigades' numbers, morale, and small arms reflect the war you've run — re-armed from the loadout you actually purchased (buy Spencers → your line carries Spencers), reinforcements included. The conditioning is **anchored exactly like the Classic-hex and auto-resolve modes** (a fresh army plays neutral; a well-run war earns up to +12%, a failing one −12%), so the three ways to fight a battle are all balanced the same.
- **A2 — fight it your way, from the bridge.** Every campaign battle's pre-battle briefing now offers **three** choices: **Auto-resolve** · **Fight in real time ⚔** (the tactical engine) · **To the Field (Classic)** (the hex battle). First Bull Run drops you into the historical scenario; every other battle generates a conditioned brigade fight. Plus a new **"⚔ SKIRMISH (custom)"** main-menu entry — pick side, army size, ground, year, and fog for a free real-time engagement.
- **A3 — the fight decides the war.** The *real* casualties you take and inflict in the real-time battle (counting the reinforcements that arrive) carry straight back: a win advances the campaign, a loss sends you into recovery, and the losses feed manpower/morale/the 1864 clock — **exactly as an auto-resolved or Classic battle would.** It's deterministic (your strategy decides it, not luck), and backing out (Esc) before the battle ends simply returns you to the briefing, re-fightable.

**Quality (the full vetting gate):** adversarial bug-hunt **46 agents → 7 root-cause defects, ALL FIXED** — the important ones: pressing **Esc on the victory screen used to silently throw the result away** (now it resolves the battle); the campaign end dialog **trapped no keyboard focus** (fixed); a **recovery role-flip was lost if you backed out and re-attempted** (now preserved until the battle truly resolves); and **reinforcements weren't getting your bought weapons** (fixed). WCAG-AA clean (the period palette carried over; 2 trivial fixes). **probe-campaign-link 16/16**; the **entire no-regression suite GREEN** (5 tactical suites + 22 strategy probes + boot/t1 + Classic still paints, 0 page errors throughout). Single file ≈**1.55 MB**. Committed + pushed (DECISIONS **D62**).

**Also this firing — historical standing instruction:** **HYBRID subagent model routing (D63)** is superseded by D145. The current rule is 5.5 for quality-critical work; helpers only get explicit model+effort bounded packets. Efficiency only where it cannot move the standard.

**⚔ PREVIOUS (this run):** TACTICAL **P1b-iii role-aware AI** (a smarter Confederate defender — closed the "AI leans Union" gap; D60) · **P1b-ii active auto-pause** (low-APM pillar, default ON; D59) · **P1b-i fog of war** (default OFF; D58) · **P1a First Bull Run** (the real battle + rail-pivot reinforcements; D57) · **P0 sandbox** (the real-time core loop; D56). Before that: **S2 m1–m5** complete (cabinet, decisions, 3-layer morale + 1864 election, press, command/named-generals).

## What's playable now (a demo click-through)
Open `civil_war_generals.html`. **Two ways in:**
1. **The owner-mode war (now end-to-end with real-time battles):** start a campaign → run the President's Desk → at each battle's **Pre-Battle Briefing**, your conditioned army is shown; click **"Fight in real time ⚔"** → fight the battle on the 3D field (drag brigades, volley, flank) → **Return to Headquarters** and your casualties + the verdict feed the campaign and advance the war. Or click **Auto-resolve** / **To the Field (Classic)** for the other two modes — all three use the same conditioned army.
2. **Free play (main menu, Field Dispatches):** **"⚔ SKIRMISH (custom)"** (pick side/size/ground/year/fog) · **"⚔ Tactical Sandbox"** · **"⚔ BATTLE — FIRST BULL RUN (1861)"**. Toggles in battle: **V** fog (default OFF), **P** auto-pause (default ON); speed 1×/2×/4×; a 2D offline fallback. The strategic desk (13 tabs, S1–S2) and Classic hex battles are unchanged.

## ⏭ NEXT (fresh chat) — PHASE B · TACTICAL DEPTH
1. **B1 the smarter ATTACKER AI** — defender-favored, fog AIDS the defender (fork #2): build the attacker to concentrate/close/assault (prototype in `ATTACKER-AI-PROPOSAL.md` + `.tmp/attacker-ai-prototype.patch`) but keep Bull Run defender-favored and **tune OUT the fog inversion** so fog stays consistent with the D58 teaching.
2. **B2** officers/command (command radius + morale bonus, can be hit) · **B3** in-battle logistics (ammo+fatigue depth + supply) · **B4** distinct arm roles (artillery canister/long-range; cavalry scout/flank/screen/raid) · **B5** difficulty/realism presets · **B6** the **CS-player "command either side" mode** (fork #10 — makes the attacker AI player-facing).
3. Then **Phase C** breadth (Eastern + Western + USCT + a custom-battle builder) → **D** full hex engine → **E** strategic S3–S5 → **H** graphics/footage/audio → **I** loot/survival → **J** polish. (Roadmap: `V1-CHECKLIST.md`.)

## Flags / open questions for Aaron
- **Phase A reuses the proven auto-resolve plumbing** (`startBattleRuntime` + `_arApplyCasualties` + `campaignAdvance`) for the feedback — so a real-time result is genuinely substitutable for the other two modes, not a parallel path. The tactical OOB is a faithful *abstraction* (a handful of brigades a side; the loss *fraction* is what feeds back), not a 1:1 regiment port — a full port is deferred (unnecessary for the layer connection).
- **CS-player Bull Run / recovery-defend re-fights** use the procedural battle for now (the fixed `bullrun1` scenario is built US-attacker); the "command either side" tactical mode is **Phase B (fork #10)**.
- **Single file ≈1.55 MB** (well within "several MB is fine"). The linked-assets/footage layer is still Phase H.

**Resume map:** `START-HERE.md` → `V1-CHECKLIST.md` (**Phase A ✅; Phase B next**) → `DECISIONS.md` **D62** (Phase A) + **D63** (model routing) + D54/D55/D61 → `MODERN-UGG-PLAN.md` → `src/tactical/` (T0 sandbox+P1b · T1 bull-run · **T2 campaign-link**) + `src/85/86/87` (the bridge) + `tools/probe-campaign-link.mjs`. Everything is on disk and pushed.
